📝 RISK DISCLAIMER

RISK DISCLAIMER

Options Trading Involves Substantial Risk of Loss — Read Carefully

IMPORTANT RISK WARNING

OPTIONS TRADING INVOLVES SUBSTANTIAL RISK OF LOSS AND IS NOT SUITABLE FOR ALL INVESTORS. YOU CAN LOSE SOME OR ALL OF YOUR INVESTED CAPITAL. NEVER TRADE WITH MONEY YOU CANNOT AFFORD TO LOSE.

# INTRODUCTION

This Risk Disclaimer ("Disclaimer") applies to all users of OnlyOptions.us ("we," "us," "our," or "OnlyOptions"). By accessing our website, subscribing to our Service, or using any information, signals, or analysis we provide, you acknowledge and accept the risks outlined in this Disclaimer.

Effective Date: February 17, 2026

Last Updated: February 17, 2026

# 1\. GENERAL OPTIONS TRADING RISKS

OPTIONS TRADING IS SPECULATIVE AND INVOLVES A HIGH DEGREE OF RISK.

Options are complex financial instruments that derive their value from underlying securities. Options trading involves risks that are different from and potentially greater than trading stocks, bonds, or other traditional investments.

## 1.1 Risk of Total Loss

YOU CAN LOSE 100% OF YOUR INVESTMENT IN OPTIONS TRADING.

Unlike stocks, which can recover over time, options have expiration dates. If an option expires out-of-the-money, it becomes worthless and you lose the entire premium paid. This can happen even if the underlying stock recovers after expiration.

Example: You buy a SPY $600 call option for $300 expiring in one week. SPY closes at $598 at expiration. Your option expires worthless. Total loss: $300 (100%).

## 1.2 Leverage Magnifies Losses

Options provide leverage, meaning small movements in the underlying security can result in large percentage gains or losses in the option position. While leverage can amplify profits, it equally amplifies losses.

Example: A 5% decline in SPY can result in a 50% loss in a call option, or even 100% if it pushes the option out-of-the-money.

## 1.3 Time Decay (Theta)

Options lose value as they approach expiration due to time decay. This loss occurs every day, regardless of whether the underlying stock moves in your favor. Short-dated options (0DTE, weekly) experience accelerated time decay.

You can be correct about the direction of a stock but still lose money if the move does not happen quickly enough to offset time decay.

## 1.4 Volatility Risk

Option prices are affected by implied volatility (IV). Changes in volatility can cause option prices to rise or fall even when the underlying stock price remains unchanged. After major events (earnings, Fed announcements), volatility often collapses, causing rapid option price declines.

# 2\. RISKS SPECIFIC TO ONLYOPTIONS.US SIGNALS

## 2.1 No Guarantee of Profits

WE DO NOT GUARANTEE ANY PROFITS, SPECIFIC RETURNS, OR TRADING PERFORMANCE.

Our historical win rate of 70.3% represents past performance only. Past performance does not guarantee future results. Market conditions change, strategies that worked previously may not work in the future, and individual trading results vary based on execution, position sizing, and risk management.

## 2.2 Individual Results Will Vary

Your actual trading results may differ significantly from our published track record due to:

•Execution timing: Signals are time-sensitive. Delayed execution results in worse entry prices.

•Bid-ask spreads: You may receive worse fills than the mid-prices we publish.

•Broker commissions: Fees reduce your net returns.

•Position sizing: Trading larger or smaller positions than recommended changes risk-reward.

•Emotional decisions: Overriding stop-losses or profit targets due to fear or greed.

•Market conditions: Rapid market moves or liquidity issues can prevent ideal execution.

## 2.3 Not Personalized Advice

ONLYOPTIONS.US DOES NOT PROVIDE PERSONALIZED INVESTMENT ADVICE.

Our signals are general educational information and market analysis. We do not know your:

•Financial situation, income, or net worth

•Risk tolerance or investment objectives

•Tax situation or legal constraints

•Time horizon or liquidity needs

•Other holdings or portfolio diversification

Signals that may be appropriate for one trader may be completely unsuitable for another. You are solely responsible for determining whether any signal is appropriate for your personal circumstances.

## 2.4 We Are Not Registered Investment Advisers

OnlyOptions.us is not a registered investment adviser (RIA) under the Investment Advisers Act of 1940. We are an educational and informational service. Our team members hold professional credentials (CMT, CFA, FINRA licenses) in individual capacities, but OnlyOptions LLC is not registered with the SEC or any state securities regulator.

We do not manage client funds, execute trades on your behalf, or provide fiduciary investment advice. Consult a licensed financial adviser before making investment decisions.

# 3\. SPECIFIC RISKS OF 0DTE (SAME-DAY EXPIRATION) OPTIONS

0DTE OPTIONS ARE AMONG THE RISKIEST TYPES OF OPTIONS TRADING.

0DTE options expire on the same day you trade them. This creates unique risks:

## 3.1 Extreme Time Decay

0DTE options lose value rapidly throughout the trading day. An option worth $2.00 at 10:00 AM can be worth $0.50 by 2:00 PM with no movement in the underlying stock. In the final hour before expiration, time decay accelerates exponentially.

## 3.2 Binary Outcomes

At 4:00 PM ET expiration, a 0DTE option is either in-the-money (has value) or out-of-the-money (worthless). There is no recovery period. Small price movements in the final minutes can determine total profit or total loss.

## 3.3 Liquidity Risk

0DTE options can experience extreme bid-ask spreads, especially far out-of-the-money strikes or during low-volume periods. You may be unable to exit a position at a fair price, or unable to exit at all.

## 3.4 Whipsaw Risk

Intraday market volatility can trigger stop-losses on trades that would have been profitable at end-of-day. 0DTE trading requires constant monitoring and fast decision-making.

## 3.5 Not for Beginners

0DTE trading requires experience, discipline, and active market-hours availability. We do not recommend 0DTE signals for:

•Traders with less than 6 months of options experience

•Traders who cannot monitor positions during market hours

•Traders with accounts under $5,000

•Traders uncomfortable with rapid, frequent losses

# 4\. HYPOTHETICAL PERFORMANCE DISCLAIMER

While our published track record reflects actual signals sent to members in real-time, the specific entry and exit prices we report are based on option mid-prices at the time of our alerts. These are hypothetical prices for the following reasons:

## 4.1 Mid-Prices May Not Represent Actual Fills

The mid-price is the average of the bid and ask price. In practice:

•Buyers typically pay closer to the ask price (higher than mid-price)

•Sellers typically receive closer to the bid price (lower than mid-price)

•During volatile markets, actual fills may be significantly worse than mid-prices

## 4.2 Slippage and Execution Delays

There is a time delay between when we send a signal and when you execute it. During this delay:

•Option prices may move against you

•The entry range may close

•Market conditions may change

Our reported results do not account for this execution lag, which is a real cost borne by traders.

## 4.3 No Commissions in Our Calculations

Our published returns are gross of brokerage commissions and fees. Actual net returns are lower after deducting:

•Per-contract commissions ($0.50–$0.65 per contract at most brokers)

•Regulatory fees (SEC/FINRA fees on sales)

•Exchange fees (on some option trades)

For high-frequency 0DTE traders, commissions can significantly reduce profitability.

## 4.4 CFTC Rule 4.41 Disclaimer

HYPOTHETICAL OR SIMULATED PERFORMANCE RESULTS HAVE CERTAIN INHERENT LIMITATIONS. UNLIKE AN ACTUAL PERFORMANCE RECORD, SIMULATED RESULTS DO NOT REPRESENT ACTUAL TRADING. ALSO, BECAUSE THE TRADES HAVE NOT ACTUALLY BEEN EXECUTED, THE RESULTS MAY HAVE UNDER- OR OVER-COMPENSATED FOR THE IMPACT, IF ANY, OF CERTAIN MARKET FACTORS, SUCH AS LACK OF LIQUIDITY. SIMULATED TRADING PROGRAMS IN GENERAL ARE ALSO SUBJECT TO THE FACT THAT THEY ARE DESIGNED WITH THE BENEFIT OF HINDSIGHT. NO REPRESENTATION IS BEING MADE THAT ANY ACCOUNT WILL OR IS LIKELY TO ACHIEVE PROFITS OR LOSSES SIMILAR TO THOSE SHOWN.

# 5\. GENERAL MARKET RISKS

## 5.1 Market Volatility

Financial markets are inherently volatile and unpredictable. Unexpected events can cause rapid, severe price movements:

•Economic data releases (jobs reports, CPI, GDP)

•Federal Reserve announcements (interest rate decisions, policy changes)

•Geopolitical events (wars, elections, trade disputes)

•Corporate events (earnings surprises, mergers, scandals)

•Black swan events (pandemics, natural disasters, systemic failures)

These events can trigger stop-losses, cause total losses on expiring options, or make positions impossible to exit.

## 5.2 Gap Risk

Stocks can gap up or down outside of market hours due to after-hours news or overnight developments. Options cannot be traded outside regular market hours (9:30 AM–4:00 PM ET). If a stock gaps against your position overnight:

•You cannot exit or adjust your position until market open

•The option may open far below your stop-loss with no opportunity to sell at the stop price

•0DTE options may open worthless after an overnight gap

## 5.3 Liquidity Risk

During periods of extreme volatility or market stress, options markets can become illiquid:

•Bid-ask spreads widen dramatically

•Market makers may withdraw, leaving no counterparty for your trade

•You may be unable to exit a losing position, forced to hold until expiration

## 5.4 Systemic Risk

In rare events (circuit breakers, exchange halts, broker technical failures), trading may be suspended entirely. You may be unable to manage risk during these periods.

# 6\. YOUR RESPONSIBILITIES AS A TRADER

## 6.1 Understand Options Before Trading

DO NOT TRADE OPTIONS IF YOU DO NOT UNDERSTAND HOW THEY WORK.

Before risking capital, you should understand:

•The difference between calls and puts

•How strike prices and expiration dates work

•What options Greeks (delta, gamma, theta, vega) mean

•How options are priced and what drives price changes

•The mechanics of buying, selling, and exercising options

•The tax treatment of options profits and losses

If you do not understand these concepts, use our education library and paper trade before using real money.

## 6.2 Only Trade With Risk Capital

NEVER TRADE WITH MONEY YOU CANNOT AFFORD TO LOSE.

Options trading capital should be:

•Money you are prepared to lose entirely without affecting your lifestyle

•Separate from emergency funds, retirement savings, or essential expenses

•Not borrowed money (margin, credit cards, loans)

•Not money needed for near-term obligations (rent, tuition, medical bills)

## 6.3 Follow Position Sizing Rules

We recommend never risking more than 2% of your account on any single trade. This rule is critical to long-term survival. Traders who ignore position sizing are the ones who blow up accounts, regardless of signal quality.

Example: With a $10,000 account, maximum risk per trade is $200. If a trade has a $0.75 per-contract risk (entry $2.40, stop $1.65), trade a maximum of 2 contracts ($150 risk). Do not trade 10 contracts ($750 risk) hoping for a bigger win.

## 6.4 Always Use Stop-Losses

IGNORING STOP-LOSSES IS THE #1 REASON TRADERS FAIL.

Every signal includes a stop-loss level. Set this as a GTC (Good Till Cancelled) limit order immediately after entering the trade. Do not:

•Override stop-losses based on hope or emotion

•Move stop-losses further away to avoid taking a loss

•Hold losing positions past expiration hoping for a miracle

Our average losing trade loses -32% because we follow stop-losses. Traders who ignore stops often turn -32% losses into -80% or -100% losses.

## 6.5 Consult a Professional

Before making any investment decisions, consult with a licensed financial adviser, tax professional, or attorney who understands your complete financial situation. We cannot and do not provide such personalized advice.

# 7\. LIMITATION OF LIABILITY

ONLYOPTIONS LLC, ITS OFFICERS, DIRECTORS, EMPLOYEES, AND AFFILIATES ARE NOT LIABLE FOR ANY TRADING LOSSES OR FINANCIAL DAMAGES ARISING FROM YOUR USE OF OUR SERVICE.

By using OnlyOptions.us, you acknowledge and agree that:

•All trading decisions are made solely by you

•You are solely responsible for any profits or losses

•We do not execute trades on your behalf or manage your capital

•We provide educational information only, not investment advice

•You will not hold us liable for any trading losses, missed opportunities, or market outcomes

This limitation of liability applies even if:

•A signal results in a total loss

•Our analysis was incorrect or incomplete

•A stop-loss was not triggered due to gap risk or liquidity issues

•You followed our signals exactly as provided

# 8\. REGULATORY AND LEGAL DISCLAIMERS

## 8.1 Not a Broker-Dealer

OnlyOptions.us is not a broker-dealer and is not registered with the SEC, FINRA, or any state securities regulator. We do not accept customer funds, hold securities, or execute trades. All trading is conducted through your own brokerage account.

## 8.2 Not Tax or Legal Advice

Information provided on our Service does not constitute tax, legal, or accounting advice. Options trading has specific tax treatment (Section 1256 contracts, wash sale rules, short-term vs. long-term capital gains). Consult a tax professional regarding your specific situation.

## 8.3 Jurisdiction-Specific Restrictions

Options trading is subject to different regulations in different jurisdictions. Some countries restrict or prohibit retail options trading entirely. It is your responsibility to ensure you are legally permitted to trade options in your jurisdiction.

Residents of certain jurisdictions (e.g., Belgium, parts of the UK under FCA restrictions) may not be eligible to trade U.S. options. Consult your local regulator before subscribing.

# INTRODUCTION

OnlyOptions LLC ("we," "us," "our," or "OnlyOptions") stands behind the quality of our Service. This Refund Policy explains when and how you can request a refund of your subscription fees.

By subscribing to OnlyOptions.us, you agree to the terms of this Refund Policy. This policy should be read in conjunction with our Terms of Service.

# 1\. 7-DAY MONEY-BACK GUARANTEE

## 1.1 Eligibility

We offer a no-questions-asked 7-day money-back guarantee on all subscription plans (Basic, Pro, and Annual).

You are eligible for a full refund if:

•You are a NEW subscriber making your FIRST payment to OnlyOptions.us

•You request a refund within 7 calendar days of your initial subscription date

•Your account has not been suspended or terminated for violations of our Terms of Service

## 1.2 What "7 Days" Means

The 7-day refund window begins at the exact time your first payment is processed and ends exactly 168 hours (7 days × 24 hours) later.

Example: If you subscribed on Monday, February 10, 2026 at 3:00 PM EST, your refund window closes on Monday, February 17, 2026 at 3:00 PM EST.

Refund requests received after the 7-day window will not be honored, even if only by minutes.

## 1.3 No Questions Asked

We do not require you to provide a reason for your refund request. Common reasons include:

•The Service did not meet your expectations

•You decided options trading is not for you

•You found a different service that better fits your needs

•You changed your mind for any personal reason

You do not need to justify your decision. Simply request a refund and we will process it.

# 2\. HOW TO REQUEST A REFUND

## 2.1 Refund Request Process

To request a refund within the 7-day window:

1.Email support@onlyoptions.us

2.Use "Refund Request" as the email subject line

3.Include your registered email address (the one you used to subscribe)

4.Optionally, include your reason (helpful for us but not required)

Example email:

To: support@onlyoptions.us

Subject: Refund Request

Body: Please process a refund for my subscription. My registered email is john.doe@example.com. Thank you.

## 2.2 Processing Time

Refunds are processed within 24–48 hours (1–2 business days) of receiving your request. You will receive an email confirmation when:

•We receive your refund request

•Your refund has been processed

Refunds are issued to your original payment method:

•Credit/debit card refunds: 3–5 business days to appear in your account (depending on your bank)

•PayPal refunds: 1–2 business days to appear in your PayPal balance

## 2.3 Access After Refund

Once your refund is processed:

•Your subscription is immediately cancelled

•Access to the Service (Discord, performance dashboard, education library) is revoked within 24 hours

•You will not be charged again unless you manually resubscribe

# 3\. WHAT IS NOT REFUNDABLE

## 3.1 Subscriptions Beyond 7 Days

NO REFUNDS AFTER THE 7-DAY WINDOW.

If you request a refund more than 7 days after your initial payment, we cannot and will not issue a refund under any circumstances, including:

•You forgot to cancel before the 7-day window closed

•You did not use the Service during your subscription period

•You experienced trading losses while following our signals

•You were too busy to evaluate the Service within 7 days

•You changed your mind after 7 days

The 7-day window is firm and non-negotiable. Plan accordingly.

## 3.2 Renewal Payments

Refunds are available ONLY for your first initial subscription payment. Renewal payments (second month, third month, etc.) are NOT eligible for refund, even if requested within 7 days of the renewal.

Example timeline:

•Day 1 (March 1): You subscribe and pay $60 → Refund eligible until Day 7 (March 7)

•Day 8 (March 8): You request refund → NOT ELIGIBLE (past 7-day window)

•Day 31 (April 1): Automatic renewal charges $60 → NOT ELIGIBLE for refund (this is a renewal payment)

To avoid renewal charges, cancel your subscription before the renewal date.

## 3.3 Trading Losses

NO REFUNDS FOR TRADING LOSSES.

We will not issue refunds, credits, or compensation based on:

•Trading losses incurred while following our signals

•Underperformance relative to our historical win rate

•Losing streaks or drawdown periods

•Signals that did not meet your profit expectations

•Individual signals that resulted in losses

Options trading involves substantial risk of loss. Our historical performance does not guarantee your results. You acknowledge this risk by subscribing to the Service. See our Risk Disclaimer for details.

## 3.4 Partial Refunds

We do not offer partial refunds or pro-rated refunds for:

•Unused days in a monthly subscription

•Time when you did not access the Service

•Cancellations mid-billing-cycle

•Downgrades from Pro to Basic plan

Refunds are all-or-nothing: either a full refund within 7 days, or no refund.

## 3.5 Free Trial Users

If you used our 7-day free trial before subscribing, you cannot request a refund on the basis of "not having enough time to evaluate the Service." The free trial provided that evaluation period at zero cost.

# 4\. REFUNDS IN SPECIAL CIRCUMSTANCES

## 4.1 Duplicate or Erroneous Charges

If you were charged twice by error or if an unauthorized charge appears on your account, contact us immediately at support@onlyoptions.us. We will investigate and issue a refund for duplicate or erroneous charges regardless of the 7-day window.

## 4.2 Technical Issues Preventing Service Access

If a technical issue on our end prevented you from accessing the Service for a significant portion of your subscription period (e.g., extended server downtime, Discord outage), contact support@onlyoptions.us. We will evaluate on a case-by-case basis and may issue a refund or credit at our sole discretion.

## 4.3 Account Termination for ToS Violations

If your account is terminated for violations of our Terms of Service (fraud, abuse, signal sharing, harassment), you are NOT eligible for any refund. All fees paid prior to termination are forfeited.

# 5\. CANCELLATION VS. REFUND — WHAT'S THE DIFFERENCE?

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Action | When to Use | What Happens |
| Cancellation | Any time, including after 7 days | Billing stops. No refund for current period. Access until end of period. |
| Refund Request | Within 7 days of first payment only | Full refund processed. Billing stops. Access revoked immediately. |

Example 1: You subscribe on March 1. On March 20 you decide to stop. You should CANCEL (not request a refund, since you are past 7 days). You keep access until March 31, then billing stops.

Example 2: You subscribe on March 1. On March 5 you realize the Service is not for you. You should REQUEST A REFUND. You get your $60 back and lose access immediately.

# 6\. CHARGEBACKS AND PAYMENT DISPUTES

## 6.1 Contact Us First

If you believe you were charged incorrectly, please contact us at support@onlyoptions.us BEFORE filing a chargeback or payment dispute with your bank or credit card company.

Most billing issues can be resolved quickly and amicably by contacting us directly. Filing a chargeback without contacting us first:

•May result in immediate account termination

•May prevent you from using the Service in the future

•Creates unnecessary delays and administrative burden

## 6.2 Valid Chargeback Reasons

We acknowledge that chargebacks are appropriate in cases of:

•Fraudulent charges (you did not authorize the payment)

•Duplicate charges caused by a technical error

•Continued billing after you cancelled (and have proof of cancellation confirmation)

## 6.3 Invalid Chargeback Reasons

Chargebacks filed for the following reasons may be disputed:

•You forgot to cancel before the renewal date

•You did not use the Service

•You experienced trading losses

•You requested a refund after the 7-day window and were denied

•You simply changed your mind after the refund period

These situations are addressed by cancellation (not chargeback). Filing a fraudulent chargeback may result in account termination and potential legal action.

# 7\. ANNUAL PLAN REFUNDS

## 7.1 Same 7-Day Window Applies

The 7-day money-back guarantee applies to Annual plan subscriptions ($600/year) in the same manner as monthly subscriptions.

If you subscribe to the Annual plan and request a refund within 7 days, you receive a FULL refund of $600.

## 7.2 No Pro-Rated Annual Refunds

If you cancel an Annual plan subscription after the 7-day window (for example, 3 months into your annual subscription), you are NOT entitled to a pro-rated refund for the unused portion.

Example: You paid $600 for an annual plan on January 1. On April 1 (3 months later) you cancel. You do NOT receive a $450 refund for the unused 9 months. You paid for 12 months of access and you will retain access for the full 12 months, but no refund is issued.

## 7.3 Recommendation

Because Annual plans are non-refundable after 7 days, we recommend:

•Start with a monthly subscription to test the Service first

•Upgrade to Annual only after you are confident in the value

•Use the 7-day free trial before committing to Annual

# 8\. CHANGES TO THIS REFUND POLICY

We reserve the right to modify this Refund Policy at any time. Changes will be effective upon posting the updated policy on our website with a new "Last Updated" date.

Refunds are governed by the Refund Policy in effect at the time of your subscription. If you subscribed under a previous version of the Refund Policy, that version applies to your refund request (if within 7 days).

# 9\. CONTACT US

If you have questions about this Refund Policy or need to request a refund, contact us:

OnlyOptions LLC

Email: support@onlyoptions.us

Subject Line: "Refund Request" (for refund requests)

Response Time: Within 24 hours during business days

We are committed to making the refund process as simple and transparent as possible. If you are within the 7-day window, we will honor your refund request promptly and without hassle.

# INTRODUCTION

This Affiliate Agreement ("Agreement") is a binding contract between you ("Affiliate," "you," or "your") and OnlyOptions LLC ("OnlyOptions," "we," "us," or "our"). By enrolling in the OnlyOptions.us Affiliate Program (the "Program"), you agree to be bound by this Agreement.

# 1\. AFFILIATE PROGRAM OVERVIEW

## 1.1 Program Purpose

The OnlyOptions.us Affiliate Program allows you to earn commissions by referring new paying subscribers to our options trading signals service. You promote OnlyOptions.us using your unique affiliate tracking link, and we pay you a commission for each successful referral.

## 1.2 Commission Structure

Affiliates earn a 30% recurring commission on all subscription revenue generated by their referred customers:

•Basic Plan ($60/month): You earn $18 per month for as long as the customer remains subscribed

•Pro Plan ($99/month): You earn $30 per month for as long as the customer remains subscribed

•Annual Plan ($600/year): You earn $180 as a one-time upfront payment

Commissions are recurring for monthly plans, meaning you continue earning $18 or $30 every month the customer renews, with no cap or time limit.

## 1.3 Lifetime Cookie

We use a lifetime cookie tracking system. Once someone clicks your affiliate link, they are tracked as your referral permanently, even if they do not subscribe immediately. If they return weeks or months later and subscribe, you still receive credit and commission.

# 2\. ENROLLMENT AND ELIGIBILITY

## 2.1 How to Enroll

To join the Program:

•Visit onlyoptions.us/affiliate

•Complete the affiliate application form with accurate information

•Await approval (typically within 2–3 business days)

•Upon approval, access your affiliate dashboard to retrieve your unique tracking link

## 2.2 Eligibility Requirements

To participate in the Program, you must:

•Be at least 18 years old

•Have a valid email address and PayPal account (or provide W-9 for direct deposit if U.S.-based)

•Not engage in prohibited marketing practices (see Section 5)

•Comply with all applicable laws and regulations

## 2.3 Application Approval

We reserve the right to approve or reject any affiliate application at our sole discretion. Reasons for rejection may include:

•Incomplete or inaccurate application information

•History of fraudulent activity or spam

•Inappropriate, unethical, or illegal website/platform content

•Prior violations of this Agreement

Rejected applicants may reapply after 90 days.

# 3\. AFFILIATE RESPONSIBILITIES AND PROMOTIONAL GUIDELINES

## 3.1 Promotional Materials

You may promote OnlyOptions.us using:

•Your unique affiliate tracking link (provided in your dashboard)

## 3.2 Accurate Representation

When promoting OnlyOptions.us, you must:

•Not guarantee specific profits or investment returns

•Include appropriate risk disclaimers when discussing options trading

Example disclosure: "This is an affiliate link. I may earn a commission if you subscribe, at no additional cost to you."

## 3.3 Brand Usage

•Use only the official logo files provided in your affiliate dashboard

# 4\. TRACKING, REPORTING, AND PAYMENTS

## 4.1 Affiliate Dashboard

You will have access to a real-time affiliate dashboard showing:

•Total clicks on your affiliate link

•Number of sign-ups and conversions

•Active subscriptions (monthly and annual)

•Commissions earned (pending and paid)

•Payment history

## 4.2 Commission Tracking

Commissions are tracked as follows:

•A user clicks your unique affiliate link and a cookie is set (lifetime cookie)

•If the user subscribes within any timeframe, you receive credit

•Commissions are credited to your account immediately upon successful payment processing

•Commissions are initially "pending" for 30 days (chargeback/refund protection)

•After 30 days, commissions are approved and available for payout

## 4.3 Payment Schedule

Payments are processed monthly according to the following schedule:

•Payment Threshold: $50 minimum balance required to receive payment

•Payment Date: Commissions approved by the 1st of the month are paid by the 15th

•Payment Method: PayPal (default) or direct deposit for U.S. affiliates

•Payment Notification: You receive an email notification when payment is sent

Example: Commissions earned in January are pending through February. On March 1st, they are approved. On March 15th, you receive payment (if balance ≥ $50).

## 4.4 Payment Methods

PayPal (Default): Payments sent to your registered PayPal email. You are responsible for any PayPal fees.

Direct Deposit (U.S. only): Available for affiliates who complete a W-9 tax form. Provide bank account details in your affiliate dashboard.

International Affiliates: PayPal is the only supported payment method. Ensure your PayPal account can receive international payments.

# 5\. PROHIBITED MARKETING PRACTICES

The following promotional methods are strictly prohibited and will result in immediate termination from the Program:

## 5.1 Fraudulent Activity

•Self-referrals: Creating accounts using your own affiliate link to earn commissions

•Cookie stuffing: Forcing affiliate cookies onto users without their knowledge

•Fake traffic: Using bots, click farms, or other artificial methods to generate clicks

•Credit card fraud: Using stolen payment methods to create fake subscriptions

## 5.2 Spam and Unsolicited Marketing

•Sending unsolicited emails (spam) promoting OnlyOptions.us

•Posting spam comments or messages on forums, social media, or blogs

•Using purchased or scraped email lists without proper opt-in consent

•Violating CAN-SPAM Act, GDPR, or other anti-spam regulations

## 5.3 Search Engine and Paid Advertising Restrictions

•Bidding on "OnlyOptions," "OnlyOptions.us," or brand misspellings in Google Ads, Bing Ads, or other PPC platforms

•Using our brand name in ad copy without explicit written permission

•Creating misleading ads that misrepresent our Service

•Using trademark-infringing domain names (e.g., onlyoptions-review.com)

## 5.4 False or Misleading Claims

•Claiming to be OnlyOptions.us or an official representative

•Guaranteeing specific profits, returns, or win rates beyond our verified track record

•Misrepresenting pricing, features, or refund policies

•Posting fake reviews or testimonials

## 5.5 Inappropriate Content

•Promoting OnlyOptions.us on websites containing illegal, adult, or offensive content

•Associating our brand with hate speech, violence, or discrimination

•Using our Service to promote pyramid schemes, MLM scams, or other unethical businesses

# 6\. REFUNDS, CHARGEBACKS, AND COMMISSION CLAWBACKS

## 6.1 Refunds

If a customer you referred requests a refund within our 7-day money-back guarantee period:

•The commission earned on that customer is reversed (clawed back)

•If the commission has already been paid to you, the amount is deducted from your next payment

•If your account balance goes negative due to clawbacks, you must settle the negative balance before receiving future payments

## 6.2 Chargebacks

If a customer disputes a charge (chargeback) and the dispute is upheld:

•All commissions related to that customer are reversed

•We reserve the right to terminate affiliates with excessive chargeback rates (>5%)

## 6.3 Cancelled Subscriptions

If a referred customer cancels their subscription:

•You stop earning commissions starting the next billing cycle

•Previously earned and approved commissions are NOT clawed back

•If the customer resubscribes later, commissions resume automatically (lifetime cookie applies)

# 7\. TERM AND TERMINATION

This Agreement begins when you are approved into the Program and continues until terminated by either party.

## 7.2 Termination by Affiliate

## 7.3 Termination by OnlyOptions

We may terminate your participation in the Program immediately, with or without notice, for:

•Violation of this Agreement (including prohibited marketing practices)

•Fraudulent activity or suspected fraud

•Excessive refund or chargeback rates

•Damage to our brand reputation

•Inactivity (no referrals or logins for 12+ months)

Upon termination by OnlyOptions for cause:

•All pending and approved commissions may be forfeited at our discretion

# DOCUMENT INFORMATION

Last Updated: February 17, 2026

EVERY EFFORT HAS BEEN MADE TO ACCURATELY REPRESENT OUR PRODUCT AND ITS POTENTIAL. THERE IS NO GUARANTEE THAT YOU WILL EARN ANY MONEY USING THE TECHNIQUES AND IDEAS IN OUR MATERIAL. EXAMPLES IN THESE MATERIALS ARE NOT TO BE INTERPRETED AS A PROMISE OR GUARANTEE OF EARNINGS.

# 1\. NO EARNINGS GUARANTEES

OnlyOptions.us does not guarantee that you will earn any money, profits, or specific returns by using our Service. Your results will vary based on:

•Your trading capital, risk tolerance, and experience level

•Your ability to follow our signals accurately and execute trades properly

•Market conditions, which are unpredictable and constantly changing

•Your discipline in following stop-losses and position sizing rules

•Broker execution quality, commissions, and slippage

# 2\. HYPOTHETICAL PERFORMANCE RESULTS

Our published track record (70.3% win rate, +87% average winner, -32% average loss) represents hypothetical results based on mid-prices at the time of our signal alerts. These are NOT actual trading results achieved by our analysts or members.

Hypothetical or simulated performance results have inherent limitations, including:

•They do not represent actual trading

•They may under- or over-compensate for market factors like liquidity

•They are designed with the benefit of hindsight

•No representation is made that any account will or is likely to achieve similar results

# 3\. MEMBER TESTIMONIALS AND RESULTS

Testimonials and earnings examples used in our marketing materials are real member-submitted results. However:

•These represent exceptional results from our most successful members

•Average member results are significantly lower

•Many members earn nothing or lose money

•Past member performance does not predict your future results

Any earnings claims or examples shown are meant to illustrate what is possible, not what is typical or guaranteed.

# 4\. TRADING INVOLVES RISK OF LOSS

Options trading involves substantial risk of loss. You can lose some or all of your invested capital. You should:

•Only trade with risk capital you can afford to lose entirely

•Never trade with borrowed money or money needed for living expenses

•Understand that our historical performance does not guarantee your results

•Consult a licensed financial adviser before making investment decisions

# 5\. YOUR SUCCESS DEPENDS ON YOUR EFFORTS

Success with OnlyOptions.us requires substantial effort on your part:

•Learning how options trading works (if you are a beginner)

•Following our signals accurately and executing trades properly

•Maintaining discipline during losing streaks

•Following risk management rules (2% position sizing, stop-losses)

•Continuously learning from wins and losses

Members who ignore these requirements typically fail, regardless of signal quality.

🛠️ OPTIONS POSITION SIZE CALCULATOR

OPTIONS POSITION SIZE CALCULATOR

Free Tool · Calculate Max Contracts · Follow the 2% Rule · Protect Your Account

# SEO METADATA

URL: /position-size-calculator

Title (58): Free Options Position Size Calculator \| 2% Rule \| OnlyOptions

Meta (157): Calculate exactly how many options contracts to trade based on your account size and risk tolerance. Free position sizing calculator using the 2% rule. Protect your capital.

Primary KW: options position size calculator

Secondary KW: how many options contracts to buy, options risk calculator, 2% rule calculator, position sizing for options

Schema: SoftwareApplication, HowTo, FAQPage

# INTRODUCTION

# Calculate Your Perfect Options Position Size in Seconds

The #1 mistake options traders make is risking too much on a single trade. Our free Position Size Calculator helps you determine exactly how many contracts to trade based on your account size, risk tolerance, and the specific option's risk parameters.

Follow the professional 2% rule: never risk more than 2% of your account on any single trade. This calculator does the math for you.

# === INTERACTIVE CALCULATOR ===

\[Developer Note: Build as interactive JavaScript calculator with real-time calculation. Below is the structure and formulas.\]

|     |
| --- |
| POSITION SIZE CALCULATOR |
| Step 1: Your Account Details<br>Account Size: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (e.g., $10,000)<br>Risk Percentage: \_\_\_\_% (default: 2%, max recommended: 3%)<br>Step 2: Option Details<br>Entry Price: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (price you plan to buy the option)<br>Stop-Loss Price: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (price you will exit if wrong)<br>Results:<br>Maximum Risk Per Trade: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>Risk Per Contract: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>Maximum Contracts to Trade: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ |

# HOW THE CALCULATOR WORKS

## The Formula

Position sizing for options follows this simple 3-step formula:

1.Calculate your maximum dollar risk: Account Size × Risk Percentage

2.Calculate risk per contract: (Entry Price - Stop-Loss Price) × 100

3.Divide to find max contracts: Maximum Dollar Risk ÷ Risk Per Contract

## Example Calculation

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Input | Value |
| Account Size | $10,000 |
| Risk Percentage | 2% |
| Entry Price | $2.40 |
| Stop-Loss Price | $1.65 |
| Calculation | Result |
| Max Dollar Risk | $10,000 × 2% = $200 |
| Risk Per Contract | ($2.40 - $1.65) × 100 = $75 |
| Maximum Contracts | $200 ÷ $75 = 2.67 → 2 contracts |

In this example, you should trade a maximum of 2 contracts. Trading 3 contracts would risk $225 (3 × $75), which exceeds your 2% limit of $200.

# WHY THE 2% RULE IS CRITICAL

## Survive Losing Streaks

Even with a 70% win rate, you will experience losing streaks. The 2% rule ensures you can survive 10, 20, or even 30 consecutive losses without destroying your account.

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Consecutive Losses | 2% Risk Per Trade | 10% Risk Per Trade |
| 5 losses | Down 9.6% | Down 41% |
| 10 losses | Down 18% | Down 65% |
| 20 losses | Down 33% | Down 88% |

With 2% risk, you can lose 20 trades in a row and still have 67% of your capital remaining. With 10% risk per trade, 20 losses destroys your account.

## Compounding Works Both Ways

Small position sizing protects you on the downside while still allowing meaningful compounding on the upside. A 70% win rate with proper sizing builds wealth slowly and safely. Oversized positions create lottery-ticket volatility.

# COMMON POSITION SIZING MISTAKES

## Mistake \#1: Ignoring the Stop-Loss

Some traders calculate position size based only on account size, ignoring where their stop-loss is. This is wrong.

Example: You have a $10,000 account and buy 10 contracts at $2.00 ($2,000 total cost). But your stop-loss is at $1.00. If hit, you lose $1,000 (10% of your account) — way over the 2% rule.

Always factor in your stop-loss distance when calculating contracts.

## Mistake \#2: Rounding Up

If the calculator tells you 2.7 contracts, trade 2, not 3. Rounding up violates the 2% rule. Always round down.

## Mistake \#3: Compounding Without Adjusting

As your account grows, your position sizes should grow proportionally. Recalculate position size on every trade based on your current account balance, not your starting balance.

Example: Start with $10,000 → 2% = $200 risk. After 3 months at $15,000 → 2% = $300 risk. Adjust up.

## Mistake \#4: Increasing Risk % After Wins

Never increase your risk percentage after a winning streak. Variance always reverts. Stick to 2% forever. If you feel invincible after 10 wins in a row, you are about to blow up.

# POSITION SIZING FOR DIFFERENT ACCOUNT SIZES

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Account Size | 2% Risk | Typical Contracts | Notes |
| $1,000 | $20 | 0-1 | Very limited. Focus on cheap options under $0.50. |
| $2,000 | $40 | 1 | Viable for weekly/monthly signals. Avoid expensive 0DTE. |
| $5,000 | $100 | 1-2 | Comfortable trading most signals. Room for 2-3 positions. |
| $10,000 | $200 | 2-3 | Sweet spot for following OnlyOptions signals actively. |
| $25,000 | $500 | 5-8 | Can trade multiple concurrent signals comfortably. |
| $50,000+ | $1,000+ | 10+ | Professional-level capital. Consider spread strategies. |

# ADVANCED POSITION SIZING TIPS

## Adjusting for Conviction

While 2% is the maximum, you can size down for lower-conviction trades:

•High conviction (3-star signals): 2% risk

•Medium conviction (2-star signals): 1-1.5% risk

•Uncertain or first time trying a strategy: 0.5-1% risk

Never size up beyond 2%, even for "sure things." There are no sure things in options.

## Portfolio Heat

Portfolio heat is your total risk across all open positions. Recommended maximum: 6-8% of account.

Example: You have 3 open trades, each risking 2%. Total portfolio heat = 6%. Do not open a 4th position until one closes.

High portfolio heat (10%+) exposes you to catastrophic drawdowns if multiple positions hit stops simultaneously.

## Scaling In

For longer-dated positions (weekly, monthly), you can split your position:

•Enter 50% of planned position immediately

•Add remaining 50% if trade moves in your favor

This reduces risk if you entered too early while maintaining upside if correct.

# POSITION SIZE CALCULATOR — FAQ

### What if the calculator gives me a fraction like 2.3 contracts?

Always round DOWN to the nearest whole number. Trade 2 contracts, not 3. Rounding up violates the 2% rule and exposes you to excessive risk.

### Can I risk more than 2% if I am very confident?

No. The 2% rule exists precisely because overconfidence kills accounts. The best trade setups can still lose. Stick to 2% maximum on every single trade, no exceptions.

### What if my account is too small to follow the 2% rule?

If your account is under $2,000, you will be limited to 1 contract per trade on most signals. This is a feature, not a bug — it protects you from overleveraging. Focus on building capital through consistent small wins rather than gambling for big scores.

### Should I adjust position size after a big win?

Yes, but only based on your new account balance, not your emotions. If you start with $10,000 and grow to $12,000, your 2% risk is now $240 instead of $200. Recalculate on every trade using your current balance.

### Do I use the premium I paid or the intrinsic value for position sizing?

Use the entry price (premium paid) minus the stop-loss price. For example, if you buy a call at $2.40 and your stop is $1.65, your risk per contract is ($2.40 - $1.65) × 100 = $75.

### What if the option gaps past my stop-loss?

Gap risk is real and unavoidable in options. This is one more reason to never exceed 2% per trade. Even if an option gaps to zero (100% loss), you only lose 2% of your account, which is recoverable. If you risked 20% and it gaps to zero, you are done.

### Can I use 3% or 5% risk if I am experienced?

Professionals rarely exceed 2%. Some experienced traders use 1% per trade (even more conservative). Increasing to 3-5% risk is gambling, not trading. Your experience does not eliminate variance — it only makes you better at discipline.

### How do I calculate position size for spreads?

For spreads, your risk is the maximum loss on the spread, not the premium paid. Example: A credit spread collected $0.50 premium with max loss of $2.00. Risk per contract = $200. With $10,000 account at 2% ($200 risk), trade 1 contract.

🛠️ OPTIONS PROFIT CALCULATOR

OPTIONS PROFIT CALCULATOR

Free Tool · Calculate Exact P&L · Project Profits Before You Trade

# SEO METADATA

URL: /options-profit-calculator

Title (55): Free Options Profit Calculator \| Calculate P&L \| OnlyOptions

Meta (158): Calculate exact profit and loss for any options trade before you execute. Enter strike, entry price, exit price, and contracts. See dollar P&L and percentage return instantly.

Primary KW: options profit calculator

Secondary KW: options P&L calculator, calculate options profit, options return calculator, how much will I make on options

Schema: SoftwareApplication, FAQPage

# INTRODUCTION

# Calculate Your Options Profit or Loss in Seconds

Know exactly how much money you will make (or lose) on any options trade before you execute it. Our free Options Profit Calculator shows you the dollar P&L and percentage return based on your entry price, exit price, and number of contracts.

Perfect for planning trades, setting profit targets, and understanding risk-reward before committing capital.

# === INTERACTIVE CALCULATOR ===

\[Developer Note: Build as interactive JavaScript calculator with real-time calculation.\]

|     |
| --- |
| OPTIONS PROFIT/LOSS CALCULATOR |
| Trade Details<br>Entry Price: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (price you bought the option)<br>Exit Price: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (price you sold or plan to sell)<br>Number of Contracts: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (default: 1)<br>Optional: Broker Fees<br>Commission per contract: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (default: $0.65, enter 0 if commission-free)<br>Results:<br>Gross Profit/Loss: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>Total Commissions: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>Net Profit/Loss: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>Percentage Return: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_% |

# HOW THE CALCULATOR WORKS

## The Formula

Options profit calculation follows this simple formula:

1.Calculate price change per contract: (Exit Price - Entry Price) × 100

2.Multiply by number of contracts: Price Change × Contracts

3.Subtract commissions: Gross Profit - (Contracts × 2 × Commission)

4.Calculate percentage return: (Net Profit ÷ Total Cost) × 100

## Example Calculation: Winning Trade

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Input | Value |
| Entry Price | $2.40 |
| Exit Price | $4.20 |
| Contracts | 3 |
| Commission | $0.65 per contract |
| Calculation | Result |
| Price Change Per Contract | ($4.20 - $2.40) × 100 = $180 |
| Gross Profit | $180 × 3 contracts = $540 |
| Total Commissions | 3 contracts × 2 sides × $0.65 = $3.90 |
| Net Profit | $540 - $3.90 = $536.10 |
| Percentage Return | ($536.10 ÷ $720) × 100 = +74.5% |

In this example, you made $536.10 net profit (74.5% return) on a $720 investment (3 contracts × $2.40 × 100).

## Example Calculation: Losing Trade

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Input | Value |
| Entry Price | $2.40 |
| Exit Price (Stop-Loss) | $1.65 |
| Contracts | 2 |
| Commission | $0.65 |
| Calculation | Result |
| Price Change | ($1.65 - $2.40) × 100 = -$75 |
| Gross Loss | -$75 × 2 = -$150 |
| Commissions | 2 × 2 × $0.65 = $2.60 |
| Net Loss | -$150 - $2.60 = -$152.60 |
| Percentage Return | (-$152.60 ÷ $480) × 100 = -31.8% |

In this example, you lost $152.60 (31.8% loss) on a $480 investment. This is within typical stop-loss parameters.

# UNDERSTANDING THE NUMBERS

## Why Options Use "× 100"

One options contract controls 100 shares of the underlying stock. This is why price movements are multiplied by 100.

Example: A $0.50 price increase in the option = $50 profit per contract ($0.50 × 100 shares).

## Commissions Matter

Commissions reduce your profit and increase your loss. The impact varies by broker:

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Broker Type | Per Contract | Round-Trip Cost (10 contracts) |
| Zero-Commission | $0 | $0 |
| Low-Cost | $0.50-$0.65 | $10-$13 |
| Traditional | $1.00-$1.50 | $20-$30 |

For active traders making 50+ trades per month, commission costs add up significantly. Zero-commission brokers (Robinhood, Webull) save money on frequent small trades.

## Percentage Return vs. Dollar Profit

Both metrics matter but serve different purposes:

•Dollar profit tells you how much actual money you made or lost

•Percentage return tells you efficiency and allows comparison across different trade sizes

Example: Making $500 on a $1,000 trade (50% return) is more capital-efficient than making $500 on a $10,000 trade (5% return).

# HOW TO USE THIS CALCULATOR EFFECTIVELY

## Before Entering a Trade

Calculate your profit targets and stop-loss outcomes before executing:

5.Enter your planned entry price

6.Calculate profit at your target price (e.g., +75% from entry)

7.Calculate loss at your stop-loss price (e.g., -30% from entry)

8.Verify your risk-reward ratio is at least 2:1

Example: If calculator shows +$180 profit target and -$75 stop-loss, your risk-reward is 2.4:1 — acceptable.

## While in a Trade

Use the calculator to evaluate partial profit taking:

Scenario: You entered at $2.40, current price is $3.60, target is $4.20.

•Calculate current profit at $3.60: +50% ($120 per contract)

•Calculate remaining profit to target: additional +17% ($60 more per contract)

•Decision: Take 50% of position off at $3.60, let 50% run to $4.20

## After Closing a Trade

Log your actual results and compare to planned outcomes:

•Was your exit price close to your planned target or stop?

•Did commissions eat more profit than expected?

•Did you achieve your planned risk-reward ratio?

This post-trade analysis improves future execution.

# REAL-WORLD SCENARIOS

## Scenario 1: SPY 0DTE Call — Quick Scalp

Entry: $1.85, Exit: $2.65, Contracts: 5, Commission: $0.65

Result: Gross +$400, Net +$393.50, Return +42.4%

Time in trade: 2 hours

## Scenario 2: NVDA Weekly Call — Swing Trade

Entry: $12.40, Exit: $21.80, Contracts: 2, Commission: $0.65

Result: Gross +$1,880, Net +$1,877.40, Return +75.7%

Time in trade: 4 days

## Scenario 3: QQQ Put — Down Market

Entry: $3.20, Exit: $5.85, Contracts: 3, Commission: $0

Result: Gross +$795, Net +$795, Return +82.8%

Time in trade: 1 day (0DTE)

## Scenario 4: Stop-Loss Hit — Losing Trade

Entry: $4.50, Exit (Stop): $3.15, Contracts: 1, Commission: $0.65

Result: Gross -$135, Net -$136.30, Return -30.3%

Outcome: Acceptable loss within 2% rule

## Scenario 5: Partial Profit — Risk Management

Entry: $2.00, Exit 50% at $3.50, Exit 50% at $4.75, Contracts: 4

First exit: 2 contracts at $3.50 = +$300 net

Second exit: 2 contracts at $4.75 = +$550 net

Total: +$850 net, Blended return +106%

# OPTIONS PROFIT CALCULATOR — FAQ

### Do I include the cost of buying the option in the profit calculation?

No. The calculator shows profit/loss from the price movement only. Your total return is automatically calculated as percentage of your entry cost. Example: Buy at $2.00, sell at $3.00 = $100 profit per contract, which is a 50% return on your $200 investment.

### What if the option expires worthless?

Enter $0.00 as the exit price. The calculator will show a 100% loss equal to your entire premium paid plus commissions. Example: Bought 2 contracts at $1.50, expired at $0 = -$300 - commissions.

### How do I calculate profit for spreads?

For spreads, calculate based on the net premium collected or paid. Example: Sold credit spread for $0.50 credit, bought back at $0.20 = $0.30 profit × 100 = $30 per spread. This calculator works for single-leg options only.

### Should I include SEC fees and regulatory fees?

You can, but they are typically small (pennies per trade). Most traders ignore them in quick calculations. For precise accounting, add them to the commission field. Example: $0.65 commission + $0.03 fees = enter $0.68.

### Why does my actual broker P&L differ slightly from this calculator?

Differences occur due to: (1) bid-ask spread (you may have filled at bid or ask instead of mid-price), (2) additional regulatory fees not included, (3) rounding in broker systems. Differences are usually under 1-2%.

### Can I use this for long-term options (LEAPS)?

Yes. The math is identical. Enter your entry price, current or projected exit price, and number of contracts. LEAPS just means longer time horizon — the P&L calculation is the same.

### What is a good percentage return for options?

This depends on time frame and strategy. 0DTE scalps: 30-60% in hours. Weekly swings: 50-100% in days. Monthly: 50-150% in weeks. Our average winning trade is +87%. Anything above 50% is considered strong.

### How do I account for early assignment risk?

This calculator assumes you close the position normally. If assigned early on a short option, you are now trading stock instead of options, and P&L calculations change. Early assignment is rare on out-of-the-money options.

# CALCULATOR IMPLEMENTATION GUIDE

\[Developer Note: Build interactive calculator with these features\]

## Input Fields:

•Entry Price (required, min: 0.01, step: 0.01, default: 2.40)

•Exit Price (required, min: 0, step: 0.01, default: 3.60)

•Contracts (required, min: 1, step: 1, default: 1)

•Commission (optional, default: 0.65, min: 0, step: 0.01)

## Validation:

•All required fields must be filled

•Entry and exit prices must be non-negative

•Contracts must be positive integer

## Calculations:

•Price Change = (Exit - Entry) × 100

•Gross P&L = Price Change × Contracts

•Total Commissions = Contracts × 2 × Commission

•Net P&L = Gross P&L - Total Commissions

•Total Cost = Entry × 100 × Contracts

•Percentage Return = (Net P&L ÷ Total Cost) × 100

## Output Display:

•Green background for profits, red for losses

•Large prominent font for Net P&L and Percentage

•Show both dollar amount and percentage

•Include a "Reset" button

## Additional Features:

•Preset scenarios: "0DTE +50%", "Weekly +75%", "Stop-Loss -30%"

•Toggle commission on/off for zero-commission brokers

•Save last calculation to localStorage

•Print/export results option

# SEO METADATA

Title (60): Free Options Trading ROI Calculator \| Monthly Returns \| OnlyOptions

Meta (158): Calculate your return on investment (ROI) for options trading. Enter starting capital and ending balance to see monthly ROI, annualized return, and compare to benchmarks.

Primary KW: options ROI calculator

# INTRODUCTION

# Calculate Your Return on Investment (ROI)

ROI measures how much profit you made relative to your capital invested. It is the single most important metric for evaluating trading performance over time. Our calculator shows monthly ROI, annualized return, and helps you track progress toward your goals.

# === INTERACTIVE CALCULATOR ===

\[Developer Note: Interactive JavaScript calculator with real-time calculation\]

|     |
| --- |
| OPTIONS TRADING ROI CALCULATOR |
| Your Trading Account<br>Starting Balance: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (account value at start of period)<br>Ending Balance: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (current account value)<br>Time Period (months): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (default: 1 month)<br>Optional:<br>Deposits Added: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (money you added during period)<br>Withdrawals: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (money you withdrew during period)<br>Results:<br>Total Profit/Loss: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>ROI %: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_%<br>Monthly ROI: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_%<br>Annualized Return: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_% |

# HOW THE CALCULATOR WORKS

## The Formula

ROI calculation accounts for deposits and withdrawals:

Adjusted Ending = Ending Balance - Deposits + Withdrawals

Net Profit = Adjusted Ending - Starting Balance

ROI % = (Net Profit ÷ Starting Balance) × 100

Monthly ROI = ROI % ÷ Number of Months

Annualized Return = Monthly ROI × 12

## Example Calculation: 3-Month Period

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Input | Value |
| Starting Balance | $10,000 |
| Ending Balance | $14,200 |
| Time Period | 3 months |
| Deposits Added | $1,000 |
| Withdrawals | $0 |
| Calculation | Result |
| Adjusted Ending | $14,200 - $1,000 = $13,200 |
| Net Profit | $13,200 - $10,000 = $3,200 |
| ROI % | ($3,200 ÷ $10,000) × 100 = 32% |
| Monthly ROI | 32% ÷ 3 = 10.7% per month |
| Annualized Return | 10.7% × 12 = 128% per year |

In this example, you grew $10,000 to $13,200 in actual profit (after accounting for the $1,000 deposit), achieving 32% total return or 10.7% monthly.

# WHAT IS A GOOD ROI FOR OPTIONS TRADING?

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Monthly ROI | Quality | Notes |
| 15%+ per month | Exceptional | Top 1% of traders. Very difficult to sustain long-term. |
| 8-15% per month | Excellent | Professional-level performance. Compound to life-changing wealth. |
| 5-8% per month | Very Good | Solid consistent profits. Most successful traders target this range. |
| 2-5% per month | Good | Profitable but modest. Better than S&P 500 (avg 10%/year). |
| 0-2% per month | Marginal | Barely profitable. May not beat buy-and-hold index funds. |
| Negative | Losing | Unprofitable. Review strategy and risk management immediately. |

# ROI BENCHMARKS AND COMPARISONS

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Investment Type | Typical Annual Return | Monthly Equivalent |
| S&P 500 Index | ~10% per year | 0.8% per month |
| Savings Account | ~1% per year | 0.08% per month |
| Conservative Options | 20-30% per year | 1.7-2.5% per month |
| Aggressive Options | 50-100% per year | 4-8% per month |
| OnlyOptions Members\* | ~72% per year (avg) | ~6% per month (avg) |

\*Based on self-reported survey of 312 active members (Nov 2025). Results vary significantly by account size, discipline, and experience.

Options trading can produce exceptional returns but also exceptional losses. The key is consistent positive ROI over many months, not huge single-month gains.

# THE POWER OF COMPOUNDING

## Monthly ROI Compounds Rapidly

Unlike annual returns, monthly returns compound 12 times per year. Small monthly gains become massive annual gains:

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Monthly ROI | After 6 Months | After 12 Months | After 24 Months |
| 3% per month | +19% | +43% | +104% |
| 5% per month | +34% | +80% | +224% |
| 8% per month | +59% | +151% | +530% |
| 10% per month | +77% | +214% | +891% |

\*Starting with $10,000

Example: $10,000 at 8% monthly ROI becomes $25,100 in 12 months and $63,000 in 24 months. This is the power of consistent compounding.

# HOW TO IMPROVE YOUR ROI

## 1\. Increase Win Rate

Going from 60% to 70% win rate (same risk-reward) significantly boosts ROI. Focus on higher-quality setups.

## 2\. Improve Risk-Reward Ratio

Targeting 3:1 instead of 2:1 on every trade increases average winner size, improving ROI even with same win rate.

## 3\. Reduce Drawdowns

The biggest ROI killer is large losing months. Follow the 2% position sizing rule religiously to avoid -20% months.

## 4\. Trade More Consistently

Skipping good setups leaves money on the table. If your system shows 2-4 signals daily, take them all (within risk limits).

## 5\. Compound Gains

As your account grows, increase position sizes proportionally. If $10K → $15K, your 2% risk is now $300 instead of $200.

# TRACKING ROI OVER TIME

## Monthly Tracking Spreadsheet

Track ROI every month in a simple spreadsheet:

|     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Month | Start | End | Profit | ROI % |
| Jan 2026 | $10,000 | $10,650 | +$650 | 6.5% |
| Feb 2026 | $10,650 | $11,400 | +$750 | 7.0% |
| Mar 2026 | $11,400 | $12,300 | +$900 | 7.9% |
| Q1 Total | $10,000 | $12,300 | +$2,300 | 23% |

## What to Look For:

•Positive ROI every month = good consistency

•ROI improving over time = learning and improving

•Large negative months = review risk management

•Erratic swings (±20%) = position sizing problem

Start: $10,000, End: $15,900, Profit: +$5,900

ROI: 59% over 6 months = 9.8% monthly average

Analysis: Exceptional. On pace for 118% annual return.

## Scenario 4: Losing Month — Drawdown

Start: $15,000, End: $13,800, Loss: -$1,200

ROI: -8%

Analysis: Significant loss. Review trades. Ensure 2% rule followed. One bad month is normal; two in a row requires action.

# FAQ

### What is a realistic monthly ROI target for options?

For most traders, 5-8% monthly ROI is excellent and sustainable long-term. This annualizes to 60-96% per year, far exceeding S&P 500. Beginners should target 3-5% monthly. Advanced traders may achieve 10%+.

### Should I count deposits and withdrawals in ROI?

Yes. If you add $1,000 mid-month and end with $11,000 (from $10,000 start), your true profit is $0, not $1,000. Always adjust for deposits/withdrawals to get accurate ROI.

### My ROI is 30% this month but -15% next month. Is this normal?

High volatility is common with options but not ideal. Aim for consistent 5-8% monthly over erratic swings. Volatility indicates inconsistent execution or poor position sizing.

### How do subscription fees affect ROI?

Subtract subscription costs from profit. Example: $600 profit - $60 OnlyOptions subscription = $540 net profit. ROI = $540 ÷ $10,000 = 5.4%.

### Can I compound my way to $1 million starting with $10,000?

Yes, mathematically. At 8% monthly ROI, $10,000 becomes $1 million in ~60 months (5 years). However, maintaining 8% monthly for 5 years is extremely difficult. Most traders experience variance.

•Monthly ROI = ROI ÷ Time Period

•Annualized = Monthly ROI × 12

🛠️ OPTIONS BREAKEVEN CALCULATOR

OPTIONS BREAKEVEN CALCULATOR

Free Tool · Calculate Breakeven Price · Know When You Profit

# SEO METADATA

URL: /breakeven-calculator

Title (59): Free Options Breakeven Calculator \| Calls & Puts \| OnlyOptions

Meta (158): Calculate the exact breakeven price for any options trade. Enter strike price and premium paid to see the stock price needed to profit. Works for calls and puts.

Primary KW: options breakeven calculator

Secondary KW: breakeven price calculator options, calculate breakeven options, call option breakeven, put option breakeven

# INTRODUCTION

# Calculate Your Breakeven Price Instantly

The breakeven price is the stock price at which your option trade neither makes nor loses money. For call options, it is strike + premium. For put options, it is strike - premium. Our free calculator does the math for both.

# === INTERACTIVE CALCULATOR ===

\[Developer Note: Interactive JavaScript calculator with call/put toggle\]

|     |
| --- |
| OPTIONS BREAKEVEN CALCULATOR |
| Option Details<br>Option Type: \[CALL\] \[PUT\] (toggle buttons)<br>Strike Price: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (the strike you purchased)<br>Premium Paid: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (price per share you paid for the option)<br>Results:<br>Breakeven Stock Price: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>Profit Above/Below: $\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (for calls: above breakeven, for puts: below breakeven) |

# HOW THE CALCULATOR WORKS

## Formulas

Breakeven calculation differs for calls vs puts:

For CALL Options:

Breakeven = Strike Price + Premium Paid

For PUT Options:

Breakeven = Strike Price - Premium Paid

## Example: Call Option Breakeven

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Input | Value |
| Option Type | CALL |
| Strike Price | $575 |
| Premium Paid | $2.40 |
| Calculation | Result |
| Breakeven Price | $575 + $2.40 = $577.40 |
| Profit Above | $577.40 (any price above this = profit) |

If SPY closes at $580, you make profit. At $577.40 exactly, you break even. Below $577.40, you lose money.

## Example: Put Option Breakeven

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Input | Value |
| Option Type | PUT |
| Strike Price | $570 |
| Premium Paid | $3.20 |
| Calculation | Result |
| Breakeven Price | $570 - $3.20 = $566.80 |
| Profit Below | $566.80 (any price below this = profit) |

If SPY falls to $560, you make profit. At $566.80 exactly, you break even. Above $566.80, you lose money.

# WHY BREAKEVEN MATTERS

## Setting Realistic Profit Targets

Your profit target should be significantly above breakeven to justify the trade.

Example: Breakeven at $577.40. Setting target at $578 (only $0.60 above breakeven) risks commissions eating all profit. Better target: $582+ ($5 above breakeven).

## Evaluating Trade Quality Before Entry

Before buying an option, ask: "How far does the stock need to move for me to profit?"

•SPY at $575, buying $575 call for $2.40 = needs to reach $577.40 (+0.4% move)

•SPY at $575, buying $580 call for $0.50 = needs to reach $580.50 (+1% move)

The $575 call is easier to profit from but costs more. The $580 call is cheaper but requires larger move.

## Time Decay Awareness

As expiration approaches, the stock must reach breakeven faster. With 5 days to expiration, SPY needs to move 0.4% to breakeven. With 1 day (0DTE), time is running out.

# BREAKEVEN VS. PROFITABILITY

## Breakeven ≠ Good Trade

Reaching breakeven is not the goal — significant profit is. Consider:

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Scenario | Stock Price | Your P&L |
| Below Breakeven | $576 | -$140 loss |
| At Breakeven | $577.40 | $0 (no gain, no loss) |
| Slightly Above | $579 | +$160 profit |
| Well Above | $582 | +$460 profit |

\*Based on $575 call, $2.40 premium, 1 contract

Aim for the "well above" scenario. The edge in options comes from large wins, not barely crossing breakeven.

# COMMON BREAKEVEN SCENARIOS

## Scenario 1: 0DTE SPY Call — Close to the Money

SPY trading at $575

Buy $575 call for $2.40

Breakeven: $577.40 (0.4% move needed)

Recommendation: High probability if SPY has upward momentum. Very achievable in one day.

## Scenario 2: Weekly NVDA Call — Out of the Money

NVDA trading at $850

Buy $870 call for $8.50

Breakeven: $878.50 (3.4% move needed)

Recommendation: Requires strong bullish catalyst. High risk, high reward.

## Scenario 3: Monthly QQQ Put — Hedge Position

QQQ trading at $480

Buy $470 put for $6.00

Breakeven: $464 (3.3% drop needed)

Recommendation: Insurance against market crash. Profitable only if significant drop occurs.

## Scenario 4: Deep ITM Call — Conservative

SPY at $575

Buy $560 call for $17.00

Breakeven: $577 (0.3% move needed)

Recommendation: High probability, but expensive. Behaves like stock with capped downside.

# HOW TO USE BREAKEVEN IN TRADE PLANNING

## Step 1: Calculate Breakeven Before Entry

Never buy an option without knowing breakeven. Run this calculator first.

## Step 2: Compare to Technical Levels

Is breakeven above or below key resistance/support?

•Breakeven at $577.40, resistance at $580 = stock may stall before you profit much

•Breakeven at $577.40, next resistance at $585 = clear path to good profit

## Step 3: Set Profit Target Well Above Breakeven

Minimum: 2× the distance from entry to breakeven.

Example: Entry at $575, breakeven $577.40 (distance: $2.40). Profit target should be at least $575 + ($2.40 × 2) = $579.80+

## Step 4: Monitor Breakeven as Time Passes

For longer-dated options, breakeven stays constant. For 0DTE, you are racing the clock — if SPY is still below breakeven 2 hours before close, exit or adjust.

# FAQ

### Does breakeven change as the option price changes?

No. Breakeven is set when you enter the trade. It equals your strike plus the premium you paid (for calls) or strike minus premium (for puts). It does not change even if the option price rises or falls.

### Do I include commissions in the breakeven calculation?

The calculator shows pure breakeven (strike + premium). To account for commissions, add them to premium. Example: $2.40 premium + $1.30 round-trip commission = $2.53 effective premium. Real breakeven: $575 + $2.53 = $577.53.

### What if I sell before expiration?

Breakeven at expiration is different from breakeven if you sell early. This calculator shows expiration breakeven. If you sell early, you profit whenever the option is worth more than you paid, regardless of the strike.

### Is it better to buy options with lower breakeven?

Not necessarily. Lower breakeven often means higher premium (more expensive). You trade capital efficiency for probability. At-the-money options have easier breakeven but cost more. Out-of-the-money options have harder breakeven but cost less.

### Can breakeven be below the current stock price for calls?

Yes, if you buy in-the-money (ITM) calls. Example: SPY at $575, you buy $570 call for $6.50. Breakeven = $576.50. The option is already profitable if SPY stays above $576.50.

# IMPLEMENTATION GUIDE

\[Developer Note: Build with these features\]

## Inputs:

•Option Type: Toggle between CALL and PUT (required)

•Strike Price (required, min: 0.01, step: 0.50)

•Premium Paid (required, min: 0.01, step: 0.01)

## Calculations:

•If CALL: Breakeven = Strike + Premium

•If PUT: Breakeven = Strike - Premium

## Validation:

•All inputs must be positive

•For puts, breakeven cannot be negative (if premium > strike, show warning)

## Display:

•Large prominent display of breakeven price

•For calls: "Stock must be above $X to profit"

•For puts: "Stock must be below $X to profit"

•Show percentage move required from current price (optional input)

# INTRODUCTION

# Track Your Win Rate — Measure Your Trading Performance

Your win rate is the percentage of trades that close profitably. It is one of the most important metrics for evaluating your trading system. Our free calculator shows your current win rate and helps you understand what percentage you need to be profitable.

# === INTERACTIVE CALCULATOR ===

\[Developer Note: Interactive JavaScript calculator with real-time calculation\]

|     |
| --- |
| WIN RATE CALCULATOR |
| Your Trading Results<br>Winning Trades: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (number of profitable trades)<br>Losing Trades: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (number of unprofitable trades)<br>Results:<br>Total Trades: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_<br>Win Rate: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_%<br>Loss Rate: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_% |

# HOW THE CALCULATOR WORKS

## The Formula

Win rate calculation is straightforward:

Win Rate = (Winning Trades ÷ Total Trades) × 100

## Example Calculation

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Input | Value |
| Winning Trades | 42 |
| Losing Trades | 18 |
| Calculation | Result |
| Total Trades | 42 + 18 = 60 |
| Win Rate | (42 ÷ 60) × 100 = 70% |
| Loss Rate | (18 ÷ 60) × 100 = 30% |

In this example, 70% win rate means 7 out of every 10 trades are profitable.

# WHAT IS A GOOD WIN RATE?

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Win Rate | Quality | Notes |
| 75%+ | Exceptional | Top-tier performance. Very difficult to maintain long-term. |
| 65-75% | Excellent | Professional-level results. OnlyOptions verified: 70.3%. |
| 55-65% | Good | Solid profitable trading with proper risk-reward. |
| 50-55% | Marginal | Barely profitable. Needs excellent risk-reward (3:1+). |
| Below 50% | Losing | Unprofitable unless risk-reward is extremely high. |

# WIN RATE BENCHMARKS BY STRATEGY

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Strategy | Typical Win Rate | OnlyOptions Verified |
| 0DTE Scalps | 60-70% | 68.2% |
| Weekly Swings | 55-65% | 72.5% |
| Monthly Swings | 50-60% | 71.8% |
| Earnings Plays | 45-55% | 64.1% |

\*OnlyOptions data from 1,847 closed signals (Jan 2023 - Feb 2026)

Win rates vary by strategy. 0DTE scalps typically show higher win rates with smaller gains. Monthly swings have lower win rates but larger average wins.

# WIN RATE VS. PROFITABILITY

## Win Rate Alone Does Not Determine Profitability

A high win rate means nothing if your average loss exceeds your average win.

Example 1: High Win Rate, Unprofitable

Win Rate: 80% (8 wins, 2 losses)

Average Win: +$50

Average Loss: -$250

Result: (8 × $50) - (2 × $250) = $400 - $500 = -$100 loss

Example 2: Lower Win Rate, Profitable

Win Rate: 50% (5 wins, 5 losses)

Average Win: +$200

Average Loss: -$75

Result: (5 × $200) - (5 × $75) = $1,000 - $375 = +$625 profit

The key is the combination of win rate AND risk-reward ratio.

## The Win Rate You Need

Required win rate depends on your risk-reward ratio:

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Risk-Reward Ratio | Breakeven Win Rate | Profitable Win Rate |
| 1:1 | 50% | 55%+ |
| 1.5:1 | 40% | 45%+ |
| 2:1 | 33% | 40%+ |
| 3:1 | 25% | 35%+ |

With a 2:1 risk-reward ratio, you only need 33% win rate to break even. At 70% win rate with 2.8:1 average ratio (our stats), expected value is strongly positive.

# HOW TO IMPROVE YOUR WIN RATE

## 1\. Follow Stop-Losses Religiously

The #1 reason win rates drop: holding losers hoping for recovery. Cut losses at your stop every single time.

## 2\. Be More Selective

Trade less, win more. Wait for high-confidence setups with 3+ confirming signals. Quality over quantity.

## 3\. Stick to Your Edge

If you win 75% on weekly SPY calls but only 50% on 0DTE TSLA, focus on SPY. Double down on what works.

## 4\. Review Every Losing Trade

Keep a trade journal. After each loss, write what went wrong. Common patterns emerge. Fix them.

## 5\. Use Limit Orders, Not Market Orders

Market orders on options get terrible fills. Limit orders improve execution, which improves win rate by 5-10 percentage points.

# TRACKING YOUR WIN RATE OVER TIME

## Sample Size Matters

Do not judge your system on 10 trades. Minimum 30 trades for preliminary assessment, 100+ for statistical confidence.

After 10 Trades:

Win rate of 80% or 40% could both be noise. Too early to conclude.

After 50 Trades:

Win rate stabilizes. If you are at 65%+, you have a working system.

After 100+ Trades:

Reliable data. Your actual skill level is now measurable.

## Monthly Tracking

Track win rate by month to identify trends:

•Is your win rate improving over time? (Good — you are learning)

•Is it declining? (Warning — review what changed)

•Does it spike/crash? (Variance — normal in small samples)

# COMMON SCENARIOS

## Scenario 1: New Trader — First Month

Trades: 15, Wins: 6, Losses: 9

Win Rate: 40%

Analysis: Below 50% but sample size too small. Continue learning. Focus on following stop-losses.

## Scenario 2: Improving Trader — Month 3

Trades: 60, Wins: 38, Losses: 22

Win Rate: 63.3%

Analysis: Good progress. On track to profitable trading. Keep doing what is working.

## Scenario 3: Experienced Trader — 6 Months

Trades: 200, Wins: 142, Losses: 58

Win Rate: 71%

Analysis: Excellent. Matches OnlyOptions verified rate. System is working.

## Scenario 4: Struggling Trader

Trades: 80, Wins: 32, Losses: 48

Win Rate: 40%

Analysis: Problem identified. Review losing trades. Likely ignoring stop-losses or taking low-quality setups.

# FAQ

### What is OnlyOptions's verified win rate?

70.3% across 1,847 closed signals since January 2023. This is calculated as: 1,298 winning trades ÷ 1,847 total trades × 100. Every signal is documented with entry/exit screenshots.

### Is 60% win rate good enough to be profitable?

Yes, if your risk-reward ratio is at least 1.5:1. With 60% wins and 2:1 risk-reward, you will be solidly profitable. With 60% wins and 1:1 risk-reward, you barely break even.

### Why is my win rate lower than 70%?

Common reasons: (1) Not following stop-losses, (2) Poor execution timing (chasing signals), (3) Trading outside your edge (low-confidence setups), (4) Broker slippage on fills. Review your trade journal to identify patterns.

### Should I count scratch trades (breakeven) as wins or losses?

Count breakeven trades (exit at entry price) as wins. If you protected capital and did not lose, that is a successful risk management outcome. OnlyOptions counts scratch trades as wins.

### My win rate is 75% but I am losing money. Why?

Your average loss exceeds your average win. You are taking profits too early and letting losers run too far. Calculate your average win vs average loss. Fix your risk-reward ratio.

### How often should I calculate my win rate?

Monthly. Track it in a spreadsheet: Month, Total Trades, Wins, Losses, Win Rate %. Review trends every quarter. Daily tracking creates emotional noise.

•Loss Rate = (Losses ÷ Total) × 100, round to 1 decimal

•Yellow background if 50-59%

•Red background if <50%
