QQQ average winner (+96%) is higher than SPY (+84%) due to greater volatility. However, win rate is slightly lower (69.4% vs 71.8%) because tech can whipsaw more unpredictably.

# QQQ TRADING STRATEGIES

## Strategy 1: Tech Earnings Momentum

Trade QQQ around major tech earnings (AAPL, MSFT, NVDA, AMZN, GOOGL).

Setup:

•Major tech earnings report due (e.g., NVIDIA earnings tomorrow)

•Buy QQQ calls if sector bullish, puts if sector bearish

•Enter 1-2 days before earnings

•Exit day after earnings (avoid IV crush if holding through)

•Target: +80-150%

Example:

Monday: NVIDIA earnings Wednesday after close, AI hype building

Signal: Buy QQQ $490 call expiring Friday for $5.20

Target: $10.40 (+100%)

Stop: $3.50 (-33%)

Outcome: NVDA beats, QQQ rallies +2.5%, exit Thursday at $11.80 (+127%)

## Strategy 2: QQQ 0DTE Breakout Plays

Trade same-day breakouts above key resistance levels.

Setup:

•QQQ consolidating below resistance (e.g., $485)

•Breakout above resistance with volume

•Buy ATM or $1-2 OTM calls

•Hold 2-4 hours

•Target: +60-100%

Example:

10:30 AM: QQQ breaks $485, surging to $486.50

Signal: Buy QQQ $487 call 0DTE for $1.80

Target: $3.20 (+78%)

Stop: $1.10 (-39%)

Outcome: QQQ reaches $490 by 2 PM, exit at $3.90 (+117%)

## Strategy 3: QQQ Put Hedges (Market Correction)

Buy puts when tech shows weakness or market fears spike.

Setup:

•Tech sector breaking down (AAPL, MSFT, NVDA all red)

•QQQ breaking support levels

•VIX spiking (fear rising)

•Buy ATM or slightly OTM puts

•Target: +80-150% (volatility expansion)

Example:

11:00 AM: Fed Chair signals rate hikes, tech plummets

Signal: Buy QQQ $482 put 0DTE for $2.40

Target: $5.00 (+108%)

Stop: $1.50 (-38%)

Outcome: QQQ drops to $478, exit put at $6.20 (+158%)

## Strategy 4: Weekly QQQ Trend Following

Ride multi-day tech trends with weekly options.

Setup:

•QQQ in clear uptrend (higher highs, higher lows)

•Tech sector leadership (NVDA, TSLA, AAPL green)

•Buy ATM calls with 5-7 days to expiration

•Hold through trend, trail stop

•Target: +70-120%

Example:

Monday: QQQ uptrending, broke $480, next target $495

Signal: Buy QQQ $482 call expiring Friday for $6.80

Target: $12.50 (+84%)

Stop: $4.75 (-30%)

Outcome: QQQ reaches $492 by Thursday, exit at $13.40 (+97%)

# QQQ CATALYSTS TO WATCH

## Events That Move QQQ

QQQ is sensitive to these catalysts:

Tech Earnings (Biggest Impact):

•AAPL, MSFT earnings can move QQQ 2-3%

•NVDA earnings (AI leader) can swing QQQ 1-2%

•AMZN, GOOGL, META also significant

Fed Announcements:

•Rate hikes = QQQ drops (growth stocks hurt)

•Rate cuts = QQQ rallies (tech benefits)

•Tech is rate-sensitive — more than SPY

Economic Data:

•Strong jobs report = tech sells off (Fed stays hawkish)

•Weak jobs report = tech rallies (Fed may cut rates)

•Inflation data (CPI, PCE) directly impacts QQQ

AI / Tech News:

•ChatGPT/AI breakthroughs = QQQ rallies

•Regulation threats = QQQ drops

•Chip restrictions (NVDA, AMD) = volatility

# QQQ OPTIONS GREEKS

## How Greeks Differ from SPY

Theta (Time Decay):

QQQ options decay faster due to higher implied volatility.

0DTE: -$0.30 to -$0.50 per day (vs SPY -$0.20 to -$0.40)

Weekly: -$0.10 to -$0.20 per day (vs SPY -$0.05 to -$0.15)

Vega (Volatility Sensitivity):

QQQ is highly vega-sensitive.

IV typically 18-25% (vs SPY 12-18%)

Spikes to 35-50% during tech sell-offs

IV crush after earnings can be severe (-30-50%)

Gamma (Delta Acceleration):

Higher gamma = bigger swings in option prices.

QQQ ATM 0DTE has gamma 0.08-0.12 (vs SPY 0.05-0.08)

Options can double or halve in value within 1 hour

# BEST TIMES TO TRADE QQQ

## Time of Day

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Time | QQQ Behavior | Best Strategy |
| 9:30-10:30 AM | Extreme volatility, wide swings | Wait for direction (avoid) |
| 10:30 AM-12:00 PM | Trends establish, best liquidity | Breakout/momentum plays |
| 12:00-2:00 PM | Consolidation, lower volume | Range-bound trades |
| 2:00-3:30 PM | Afternoon tech rally/sell-off | Trend continuation |
| 3:30-4:00 PM | Wild swings, gamma explosion | Close all 0DTE positions |

## Best Days for QQQ Trades

•Wednesday-Friday: Tech earnings concentrated mid-week

•First Friday of month: Jobs report → high volatility

•FOMC days: Fed announcements create 2-3% QQQ moves

•Avoid: Holiday-shortened weeks (low volume, erratic)

# QQQ VS SPY — WHICH SHOULD YOU TRADE?

## Decision Matrix

Trade QQQ if you:

•Have 6+ months options experience

•Can handle higher volatility and faster price swings

•Prefer aggressive, high-reward trades

•Are bullish on tech sector specifically

•Have larger account ($5,000+) to absorb bigger losses

Trade SPY if you:

•Are a beginner (<6 months experience)

•Want lower volatility and steadier gains

•Prefer conservative, predictable setups

•Have smaller account ($2,000-$5,000)

•Want higher win rate (SPY 71.8% vs QQQ 69.4%)

OnlyOptions Recommendation:

Start with SPY for first 3-6 months. Once profitable and comfortable, add QQQ to your playbook for 30-40% of trades. Diversifying between SPY and QQQ provides balance.

# COMMON QQQ MISTAKES

Mistake #1: Underestimating Volatility

You size QQQ positions like SPY. QQQ moves 2x faster, so your stop-loss gets hit 2x more often. Use tighter position sizing (1.5% risk instead of 2%).

Mistake #2: Holding Through Tech Earnings Without Plan

You hold a QQQ call through AAPL earnings hoping for a pop. AAPL beats but QQQ drops due to other tech weakness. Exit before earnings or use defined-risk spreads.

Mistake #3: Ignoring Sector Rotation

Tech is out of favor (money rotating to energy, financials). You keep buying QQQ calls because "tech always goes up." It does not. Follow sector trends.

Mistake #4: Buying QQQ Puts in Strong Bull Markets

QQQ in a raging bull trend. You buy puts thinking it is "too high" and must correct. You lose -80%. Trade with the trend, not against it.

# FAQ

### Is QQQ riskier than SPY?

Yes. QQQ has higher volatility (18-25% IV vs SPY 12-18%), concentrated in 100 stocks vs 500, and heavy tech exposure. This creates bigger swings — both up and down. Only trade QQQ if you can handle volatility.

### Can beginners trade QQQ options?

Not recommended for absolute beginners. Start with SPY for first 3-6 months. Once you have 20+ profitable trades and understand volatility, add QQQ. QQQ punishes mistakes harder than SPY.

### Why does QQQ sometimes drop when SPY is flat?

QQQ is tech-heavy. If tech stocks (AAPL, MSFT, NVDA) are weak while energy/financials are strong, SPY stays flat but QQQ drops. This is sector rotation. Check QQQ vs SPY correlation before trading.

### What is the best QQQ option expiration?

Depends: 0DTE for scalps (2-4 hours), weekly for swing trades (2-5 days), monthly for trend following (1-3 weeks). 50% of our QQQ signals are weekly options for balance of time and volatility.

### Does QQQ follow NASDAQ futures?

Yes, closely. NASDAQ futures (NQ) trade 23 hours/day. Check NQ futures at 9:00 AM before market open to predict QQQ opening direction. If NQ up +0.5%, expect QQQ to open higher.

### When should I trade QQQ puts instead of calls?

Trade puts when: (1) Tech sector breaking support, (2) Fed hawkish (rate hikes hurt tech), (3) VIX spiking >25, (4) Major tech earnings disappoint. Otherwise, default to calls — QQQ trends up long-term.

📝 HOW TO GET APPROVED FOR OPTIONS TRADING

HOW TO GET APPROVED FOR OPTIONS TRADING

Complete Guide to Options Approval at Every Broker

SEO METADATA

URL: /how-to-get-approved-for-options-trading

Title (60): How to Get Approved for Options Trading \| Approval Guide 2026

Meta Description (159): Learn how to get approved for options trading at any broker. Understand approval levels, application process, requirements, tips to get approved fast, and what to do if denied.

Primary KW: how to get approved for options trading

Secondary KW: options trading approval, options approval levels, get options approved, options account approval, apply for options trading

INTRODUCTION

Getting Options Approval is Easier Than You Think

Before you can trade options, your broker must approve your account for options trading. This process involves answering questions about your financial situation, investment experience, and understanding of risk.

Most brokers approve Level 1 options (buying calls and puts) within minutes to 24 hours. This guide shows you exactly how to apply, what to say, and how to get approved quickly.

OPTIONS APPROVAL LEVELS EXPLAINED

The 5 Approval Levels

Brokers categorize options approval into levels based on risk:

Level        What You Can Do        Risk        Who Needs It

Level 1        Buy calls and puts (covered calls)        Low (max loss = premium)        Beginners, 90% of traders

Level 2        Everything in Level 1 + spreads        Low-Moderate        Intermediate traders

Level 3        Sell naked puts (cash-secured)        Moderate        Experienced traders

Level 4        Sell naked calls (unlimited risk)        High        Advanced traders

Level 5        Index options, futures options        Very High        Professionals

For OnlyOptions Signals:

You only need Level 1 approval. All our signals are buying calls or puts — the safest category. Never apply for higher levels unless you understand the risks.

APPLICATION PROCESS — STEP BY STEP

Step 1: Log Into Your Broker Account

Open your existing brokerage account or create a new one.

Step 2: Find the Options Application

Location varies by broker:

•        Robinhood: Account → Settings → Investing → Options Trading

•        Webull: Account → More → Options Trading Application

•        Thinkorswim (TD Ameritrade): My Account → General → Elections & Routing → Option Trading

•        E\*TRADE: Accounts → Options Trading → Apply

•        Fidelity: Accounts & Trade → Update Accounts/Features → Apply for Options

Step 3: Answer Personal Information Questions

These are standard for all brokers:

Employment Status:

•        Employed, Self-Employed, Retired, Student, or Unemployed

•        Answer honestly

Annual Income:

•        Typical ranges: <$25K, $25-50K, $50-100K, $100K+

•        Tip: Higher income increases approval odds, but be truthful

Net Worth:

•        Total assets minus liabilities

•        Includes: savings, investments, home equity

•        Excludes: retirement accounts (sometimes)

Liquid Net Worth:

•        Cash and investments (excluding real estate)

•        Example: $20K in savings + $15K in stocks = $35K liquid

Step 4: Answer Investment Experience Questions

This is where approval is won or lost. Be strategic:

Q: How long have you been investing?

Best answer: 1-3 years or 3-5 years (shows experience without overcommitting)

Acceptable: 6 months - 1 year (acceptable for Level 1)

Risky: None/Less than 6 months (may get denied)

Q: How many trades do you make per year?

Best answer: 10-50 trades (shows active interest)

Acceptable: 5-10 trades

Risky: 0 trades (no experience)

Q: Options trading experience?

Best answer: 1-3 years (if true)

Acceptable: Less than 1 year OR "limited knowledge" (fine for Level 1)

Important: Do NOT select "No experience" if possible — select "limited knowledge" instead

Q: What is your investment objective?

Best answer: "Income" or "Growth" (conservative)

Acceptable: "Speculation" (shows you understand risk)

Risky: "Capital Preservation" (too conservative for options)

Step 5: Answer Options Knowledge Questions

Some brokers (Thinkorswim, Fidelity) test your knowledge:

Q: Do you understand that options can expire worthless?

Answer: YES (always)

Q: Do you understand options are leveraged instruments?

Answer: YES

Q: What is the maximum loss when buying a call option?

Correct Answer: The premium paid (limited loss)

Q: What is the maximum gain when buying a call option?

Correct Answer: Unlimited (as stock rises)

Step 6: Select Your Desired Approval Level

Choose Level 1 only:

•        ✓ Covered Calls

•        ✓ Cash-Secured Puts

•        ✓ Buy Calls and Puts to Open

Do NOT check Level 2, 3, or 4 unless you specifically need them. Applying for higher levels may delay approval or trigger phone verification.

Step 7: Read and Agree to Disclosures

Check all boxes confirming:

•        You understand options involve risk

•        You have read the Options Disclosure Document (ODD)

•        You agree to the terms

Step 8: Submit Application

Click "Submit" and wait for approval.

Approval Timeline:

•        Robinhood: Instant (under 60 seconds) for Level 1

•        Webull: 1-2 business days

•        Thinkorswim: 1-3 business days

•        E\*TRADE: 1-2 business days

•        Fidelity: 1-3 business days

•        Schwab: 1-3 business days

TIPS TO GET APPROVED FASTER

1\. Answer Consistently

Do not contradict yourself. If you say you have 2 years investing experience, do not say 0 options trades. Say 5-10 trades minimum.

2\. Show Some Experience

Even if you are a beginner, answer "Limited knowledge" instead of "No knowledge." Brokers want to see you have done basic research.

3\. Have Adequate Liquid Net Worth

Level 1 approval is easier with $10,000+ liquid net worth. If you have less, emphasize income instead.

4\. Apply for Level 1 Only

Do not get greedy and apply for Level 3 or 4 on your first application. Get Level 1 approved, trade for 6 months, then upgrade if needed.

5\. Use Real Information

Brokers may verify income, employment, or net worth. Do not lie. Exaggerating slightly is normal (everyone does), but outright fabrication can get your account closed.

WHAT IF YOU GET DENIED?

Reasons for Denial

Common reasons brokers deny options approval:

•        Insufficient income or net worth (<$25K combined)

•        No investment experience (selected "None" or "0 trades")

•        Application inconsistencies (said 5 years experience but 0 trades)

•        Applied for too high a level (Level 3 or 4 as beginner)

What to Do if Denied

Option 1: Reapply in 30-90 Days

Wait 1-3 months, then reapply. Update your answers:

•        Increase experience (you now have 6 months investing)

•        Increase trades ("I made 10 trades since last application")

•        Adjust net worth if you saved more money

Option 2: Call Broker Support

Call and ask: "Why was I denied? What do I need to get approved?"

They may approve you over the phone after verifying information.

Option 3: Switch Brokers

Some brokers are easier than others:

•        Robinhood: Easiest (instant approval for most)

•        Webull: Easy (low requirements)

•        Thinkorswim: Moderate (slightly stricter)

•        Fidelity/Schwab: Moderate to Hard (conservative)

If denied at Fidelity, try Robinhood or Webull.

Option 4: Trade in an IRA

Some brokers approve options in IRAs more easily than taxable accounts. Apply for IRA options approval as alternative.

UPGRADING TO HIGHER LEVELS

When to Upgrade

After 6-12 months of successful Level 1 trading, you may want Level 2 for spreads (vertical spreads, iron condors). Only upgrade if you understand the strategies.

How to Upgrade

1.        Log into broker account

2.        Navigate to Options Trading settings

3.        Select "Upgrade Options Level"

4.        Answer updated experience questions (now you have 1+ year experience)

5.        Submit

Upgrades are usually approved faster than initial applications (1-2 days).

BROKER-SPECIFIC APPROVAL GUIDES

Robinhood

Approval Process: Instant (under 60 seconds)

Requirements: Age 18+, no minimum income/net worth

Difficulty: Easiest

Notes: Nearly everyone gets approved for Level 1 instantly. If denied, likely due to account restrictions or flags.

Webull

Approval Process: 1-2 business days

Requirements: $2,000 recommended net worth, some investment experience

Difficulty: Easy

Notes: Answer "1-3 years experience" and "10-50 trades" for fast approval.

Thinkorswim (TD Ameritrade)

Approval Process: 1-3 business days

Requirements: $5,000+ liquid net worth recommended, investment experience

Difficulty: Moderate

Notes: May require phone call for Level 3+. Level 1 and 2 approved online.

E\*TRADE

Approval Process: 1-2 business days

Requirements: $3,000+ net worth, some experience

Difficulty: Moderate

Notes: Conservative broker but approves most Level 1 applications.

Fidelity

Approval Process: 1-3 business days

Requirements: $10,000+ net worth recommended, documented experience

Difficulty: Moderate-Hard

Notes: More conservative. May deny applicants with no trading history.

Charles Schwab

Approval Process: 1-3 business days

Requirements: $5,000+ net worth, experience

Difficulty: Moderate

Notes: Similar to E\*TRADE. Approves most legitimate applications.

FAQ

Do I need a certain amount of money in my account?

No minimum deposit required for options approval at most brokers. However, higher account balances ($2,000+) improve approval odds. You can deposit money after approval.

Can I get approved with no trading experience?

Difficult but possible. At Robinhood, yes (instant approval). At other brokers, select "Limited knowledge" instead of "None" and answer that you have done research. Emphasize willingness to learn.

Will my employer know I applied for options?

No. Brokers do not contact your employer. However, if you work in finance (FINRA-regulated), your employer may monitor your trading activity per compliance rules.

Can I trade options in my IRA or retirement account?

Yes, most brokers allow Level 1 options (buying calls/puts) in IRAs. Apply separately for IRA options approval. Higher levels (Level 3+) often restricted in retirement accounts.

What happens if I lie on my application?

Brokers may verify information. If caught, your account can be frozen or closed. Be honest. Slight exaggeration is normal, but do not fabricate income, net worth, or experience entirely.

How long does Level 1 approval last?

Indefinitely. Once approved, you remain approved unless you violate terms (pattern day trading without $25K, fraud, etc.). No renewal required.

Can I get approved if I am under 18?

No. You must be 18+ (or legal age in your country) to trade options. Minors cannot open options accounts even with parental consent at most brokers.

Do I need to take a test to get approved?

No formal test. Some brokers (Thinkorswim, Fidelity) ask knowledge questions, but they are basic (max loss, max gain). If you read this guide, you can answer them correctly.

📝 POSITION SIZING GUIDE FOR OPTIONS

POSITION SIZING GUIDE FOR OPTIONS

Master the 2% Rule and Protect Your Capital

# SEO METADATA

URL: /position-sizing-guide-options

Title (59): Position Sizing Guide for Options: 2% Rule Explained 2026

Meta Description (157): Learn proper position sizing for options trading. Master the 2% rule, calculate max contracts, adjust for account growth, and avoid the #1 mistake that destroys accounts.

Primary KW: position sizing options

Secondary KW: 2% rule options, how many contracts to buy, position sizing calculator, options position size

# INTRODUCTION

Position Sizing is THE Difference Between Success and Failure

You can have a 70% win rate and still blow up your account with poor position sizing. You can have a 50% win rate and become wealthy with perfect position sizing. It is that important.

This guide teaches you the 2% rule, how to calculate exact position sizes, and how to adjust as your account grows.

# THE 2% RULE — FOUNDATION OF POSITION SIZING

## What is the 2% Rule?

Never risk more than 2% of your total account value on any single trade. This is measured as the maximum dollar amount you will lose if your stop-loss is hit.

Example:

Account size: $10,000

2% risk: $200 maximum loss per trade

If stop-loss is hit, you lose $200 (not more, not less)

## Why 2% (Not 5% or 10%)?

The math is simple: survive losing streaks.

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Risk Per Trade | 10 Losses | 20 Losses | Account Left |
| 2% | Down 18% | Down 33% | $6,700 ✓ |
| 5% | Down 40% | Down 64% | $3,600 |
| 10% | Down 65% | Down 88% | $1,200 ✗ |

With 2% risk, even 20 straight losses (virtually impossible with 70% win rate) only costs 33% of your account. You can recover. With 10% risk, you are destroyed.

# CALCULATING POSITION SIZE — STEP BY STEP

## The Formula

Position size calculation has 3 steps:

Step 1: Calculate Maximum Dollar Risk

Max Risk = Account Size × 2%

Example: $10,000 × 0.02 = $200

Step 2: Calculate Risk Per Contract

Risk Per Contract = (Entry Price - Stop-Loss Price) × 100

Example: ($2.40 - $1.65) × 100 = $75 per contract

Step 3: Calculate Maximum Contracts

Max Contracts = Max Risk ÷ Risk Per Contract

Example: $200 ÷ $75 = 2.67 → Trade 2 contracts (always round down)

## Complete Example

Account: $10,000

Signal: SPY $575 call, entry $2.30-$2.50, stop-loss $1.65

You enter at $2.40

Step 1: Max Risk = $10,000 × 2% = $200

Step 2: Risk Per Contract = ($2.40 - $1.65) × 100 = $75

Step 3: Max Contracts = $200 ÷ $75 = 2.67

Decision: Trade 2 contracts (not 3)

Why not 3? Because 3 × $75 = $225 risk, which exceeds your $200 limit. Always round down.

# POSITION SIZING BY ACCOUNT SIZE

|     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Account Size | 2% Risk | Typical Signal | Max Contracts | Notes |
| $1,000 | $20 | $75 risk | 0 (skip) | Too small |
| $2,000 | $40 | $75 risk | 0 (skip) | Minimum viable |
| $5,000 | $100 | $75 risk | 1 | Good for beginners |
| $10,000 | $200 | $75 risk | 2 | Ideal starting point |
| $25,000 | $500 | $75 risk | 6 | Comfortable sizing |
| $50,000 | $1,000 | $75 risk | 13 | Professional level |

Key Insight:

Small accounts ($1,000-$2,000) struggle with position sizing. You often cannot take signals because 2% risk does not cover one contract. This is why we recommend $5,000 minimum for comfortable trading.

# ADJUSTING POSITION SIZE AS ACCOUNT GROWS

## Compound Your Gains

As your account grows, your position sizes grow automatically. This is how you accelerate wealth.

Example Progression:

Month 1: Account $10,000 → 2% risk = $200 → Trade 2 contracts

Month 3: Account $12,000 → 2% risk = $240 → Trade 3 contracts

Month 6: Account $15,000 → 2% risk = $300 → Trade 4 contracts

Month 12: Account $20,000 → 2% risk = $400 → Trade 5 contracts

You are trading larger positions without increasing risk percentage. This is compounding in action.

## Recalculate After Every 10% Growth

Update your position sizes when account grows 10%+:

•$10,000 → $11,000: Recalculate (now $220 max risk)

•$11,000 → $12,100: Recalculate (now $242 max risk)

•Continue this pattern as account compounds

# POSITION SIZING FOR DIFFERENT STRATEGIES

## 0DTE Options — Use 1% Risk (Not 2%)

0DTE is riskier due to extreme time decay and binary outcomes. Reduce position size to 1% of account.

Example:

Account: $10,000

0DTE signal risk: $75 per contract

Use 1% rule: $100 max risk

Max contracts: 1 (not 2)

## Weekly/Monthly Options — Standard 2%

Weekly and monthly options allow standard 2% risk. More time to expiration = less risk of total loss.

## High-Confidence Signals — Still 2%

Even on our highest-confidence 3-star signals, never exceed 2% risk. Confidence does not eliminate risk. Stick to the rule.

# PORTFOLIO HEAT MANAGEMENT

## What is Portfolio Heat?

Total dollar amount at risk across all open positions simultaneously.

Example:

Position 1: Risk $200 (SPY call)

Position 2: Risk $150 (QQQ put)

Position 3: Risk $180 (NVDA call)

Total portfolio heat: $530 (5.3% of $10,000 account)

## Maximum Portfolio Heat: 8%

Never have more than 8% total portfolio heat at once. This prevents correlated positions from wiping you out simultaneously.

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Portfolio Heat | Action |
| 0-4% | Low risk. Room for more positions. |
| 4-6% | Balanced. Ideal range. |
| 6-8% | High. Maximum recommended. |
| 8%+ | Dangerous. Do NOT open new positions. |

# POSITION SIZING BY CONVICTION LEVEL

## Not All Signals Are Equal

OnlyOptions rates signals by confidence (3-star, 2-star, 1-star). Adjust position size accordingly:

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Signal Confidence | Risk % | Example ($10K) |
| 3-Star (High) | 2% | $200 max |
| 2-Star (Medium) | 1-1.5% | $100-$150 max |
| 1-Star (Low) | 0.5-1% | $50-$100 max |

This allows you to bet more on high-probability setups and less on speculative plays.

# COMMON POSITION SIZING MISTAKES

## Mistake \#1: Rounding Up Instead of Down

Calculation: 2.67 contracts

Wrong: Trade 3 contracts ("close enough")

Right: Trade 2 contracts

Why: 3 contracts exceeds your risk limit. Always round down.

## Mistake \#2: Ignoring Stop-Loss in Calculation

You calculate position size based on entry price only, forgetting the stop-loss. This leads to massive oversizing. Always use entry - stop in your calculation.

## Mistake \#3: Using 2% of Position Value Instead of Account

Wrong: "I will risk 2% of this $500 trade = $10 stop"

Right: "I will risk 2% of my $10,000 account = $200 stop"

2% applies to total account, not individual position.

## Mistake \#4: Not Adjusting for Account Growth

Your account grows from $10,000 to $15,000. You still trade 2 contracts because "that is what I always do." You are leaving money on the table. Recalculate regularly.

## Mistake \#5: Increasing Risk After Big Wins

You hit 3 winners in a row. You think "I am hot, time to go big" and risk 5% per trade. Variance always reverts. Stick to 2% always.

# POSITION SIZING FOR SMALL ACCOUNTS

## The $1,000-$5,000 Problem

Small accounts face position sizing challenges:

•2% of $2,000 = $40 max risk

•Typical signal risk = $75 per contract

•Result: Cannot take most signals

## Solutions

Option 1: Save More Before Trading

Wait until you have $5,000+ before starting. This gives you $100 risk (1 contract on most signals).

Option 2: Take Only Low-Cost Signals

Focus on 0DTE signals with $0.25-$0.50 entry prices. Risk per contract = $15-$25. Fits small accounts.

Option 3: Paper Trade Until Account Grows

Use paper trading while saving. Once you hit $5,000, start with real money.

# FAQ

### What if I cannot afford even 1 contract at 2% risk?

Skip that trade. Do not violate the 2% rule to force a position. Wait for a lower-cost signal or save more capital. Trading with insufficient capital destroys accounts.

### Can I use 3% or 5% risk if I am confident?

No. Confidence is irrelevant. Even our 3-star signals lose 30% of the time. Stick to 2% always. The rule exists to protect you from yourself.

### Should I reduce position size after a losing streak?

No. Your position size is based on current account value, which already reflects losses. If account drops from $10,000 to $9,000, your 2% risk automatically reduces from $200 to $180.

### What if my calculated position is a fraction like 1.3 contracts?

Always round down to 1 contract. You cannot trade partial contracts on most brokers. Rounding up violates the 2% rule.

### How do I position size for spreads?

Use the maximum possible loss on the spread (not the premium paid). Example: Bull call spread max loss is $200, that is your risk per contract for position sizing.

### Should I use 2% on every signal, even low-conviction ones?

You can use less (1-1.5%) on low-conviction signals, but never more than 2% on any signal regardless of conviction. Adjust down, never up.

📝 UNDERSTANDING OPTIONS PREMIUM PRICING

UNDERSTANDING OPTIONS PREMIUM PRICING

Complete Guide to What Determines Option Prices

# SEO METADATA

URL: /understanding-options-premium-pricing

Title (60): Options Premium Pricing Explained: Complete Guide 2026

Meta Description (159): Learn what determines options premium prices: intrinsic value, time value, the 6 factors that affect pricing, and why options cost what they cost. Complete guide with examples.

Primary KW: options premium pricing

Secondary KW: what determines option price, intrinsic vs extrinsic value, why options cost, option pricing factors

# INTRODUCTION

# Why Does This Option Cost $2.40?

You see an option priced at $2.40 ($240 per contract). But why $2.40? Why not $1.20 or $4.80? What forces determine this price?

Options prices are not random. They are calculated based on 6 key factors. Understanding these factors helps you identify cheap vs expensive options and make smarter trading decisions.

# THE TWO COMPONENTS OF OPTION PREMIUM

## Every Option Price Has Two Parts

Option Premium = Intrinsic Value + Extrinsic Value (Time Value)

Formula:

Total Premium = What It's Worth Now + What It Might Be Worth Later

## Intrinsic Value (Real Value)

Intrinsic value is how much the option is "in-the-money" right now. It is the profit you would make if you exercised the option immediately.

Formulas:

Call Intrinsic Value = Stock Price - Strike Price (if positive)

Put Intrinsic Value = Strike Price - Stock Price (if positive)

Example - Calls:

Stock: $575 (SPY)

$570 call: Intrinsic = $575 - $570 = $5.00 (in-the-money)

$575 call: Intrinsic = $575 - $575 = $0.00 (at-the-money)

$580 call: Intrinsic = $0 (out-of-the-money, can't be negative)

Example - Puts:

Stock: $575 (SPY)

$580 put: Intrinsic = $580 - $575 = $5.00 (in-the-money)

$575 put: Intrinsic = $575 - $575 = $0.00 (at-the-money)

$570 put: Intrinsic = $0 (out-of-the-money)

## Extrinsic Value (Time Value)

Extrinsic value is the "hope premium" — what traders pay for the possibility the option will gain intrinsic value before expiration.

Formula:

Extrinsic Value = Total Premium - Intrinsic Value

Example:

SPY at $575, $575 call trading at $4.20, 7 days to expiration

Intrinsic value: $575 - $575 = $0.00 (at-the-money)

Extrinsic value: $4.20 - $0.00 = $4.20

All premium is extrinsic (time value)

Another Example:

SPY at $580, $575 call trading at $8.50, 7 days to expiration

Intrinsic value: $580 - $575 = $5.00

Extrinsic value: $8.50 - $5.00 = $3.50

Premium breakdown: $5.00 intrinsic + $3.50 extrinsic

## Visual Breakdown Table

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Option | Total Premium | Intrinsic | Extrinsic |
| SPY $570 call (ITM) | $9.20 | $5.00 | $4.20 |
| SPY $575 call (ATM) | $4.20 | $0.00 | $4.20 |
| SPY $580 call (OTM) | $1.80 | $0.00 | $1.80 |

Key insight: Out-of-the-money and at-the-money options are 100% extrinsic value (pure time value). In-the-money options have both components.

# THE 6 FACTORS THAT DETERMINE OPTION PRICE

## Factor 1: Stock Price vs Strike Price

The closer the stock price to the strike, the more expensive the option.

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Strike (SPY at $575) | Call Premium | Moneyness |
| $570 (ITM) | $9.20 | $5 in-the-money |
| $575 (ATM) | $4.20 | At-the-money |
| $580 (OTM) | $1.80 | $5 out-of-the-money |
| $585 (OTM) | $0.65 | $10 out-of-the-money |

Every $1 move in stock price changes option price by Delta (e.g., Delta 0.50 = $0.50 change per $1 stock move).

## Factor 2: Time to Expiration

More time = higher premium. Time value decays as expiration approaches.

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Time to Expiration | SPY $575 Call Premium |
| 0 days (0DTE) | $1.80 |
| 7 days (weekly) | $4.20 |
| 30 days (monthly) | $9.50 |
| 60 days | $13.20 |
| 90 days | $16.00 |

Notice: Doubling time (7→14 days) does NOT double price. Time value decays faster as expiration nears (theta).

## Factor 3: Implied Volatility (IV)

Higher volatility expectation = higher premium. IV is the biggest driver of extrinsic value.

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Implied Volatility | SPY $575 Call (7 days) |
| Low IV (12%) | $3.50 |
| Normal IV (18%) | $4.20 |
| High IV (25%) | $6.80 |
| Extreme IV (35%) | $9.20 |

Same option, same stock price, but premium nearly 3x higher with high IV. This is why checking IV before buying is critical.

## Factor 4: Interest Rates

Higher interest rates slightly increase call premiums and decrease put premiums. Small effect (1-3%) compared to other factors.

Why: Buying calls is like borrowing money to control stock. Higher rates = slightly more expensive calls.

## Factor 5: Dividends

Expected dividends decrease call premiums and increase put premiums slightly. Only matters for stocks with large dividends (>2% yield).

Why: Stock drops on ex-dividend date. Calls lose value, puts gain value from the drop.

## Factor 6: Supply and Demand

If everyone is buying calls, premiums rise above theoretical value. If everyone is selling, premiums fall below theoretical value.

This is why options on highly traded stocks (SPY, AAPL) have tighter pricing than illiquid stocks.

# HOW OPTIONS ARE PRICED: BLACK-SCHOLES MODEL

## The Pricing Formula

Options are priced using mathematical models (Black-Scholes being most famous). You do not need to calculate this — your broker does it automatically.

Inputs to Black-Scholes:

•Current stock price

•Strike price

•Time to expiration

•Implied volatility

•Risk-free interest rate

•Expected dividends

Output:

Theoretical fair value of the option (e.g., $4.23)

Market price may differ slightly from theoretical price due to supply/demand, but usually within 2-5%.

## Why You Don't Need to Calculate

Your broker shows you the price. Market makers calculate fair value using advanced models. Your job: Understand what makes prices move up or down, not calculate exact values.

# WHY OPTIONS LOSE VALUE OVER TIME

## Time Decay (Theta) Explained

Extrinsic value decreases every day as expiration approaches. This is time decay or theta.

Example: 30-Day Option

Day 1: Premium $9.50 (all extrinsic)

Day 10: Premium $8.20 (lost $1.30 to theta)

Day 20: Premium $6.10 (lost $2.10 more)

Day 27: Premium $3.50 (lost $2.60 more — accelerating)

Day 30: Expires $0 if out-of-the-money

Key Insight:

Theta accelerates in final 7 days. An option loses 50% of remaining extrinsic value in last 3 days. This is why holding to expiration is dangerous.

## Theta by Time to Expiration

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Days Left | Daily Theta (Approx) |
| 30+ days | -$0.03 to -$0.05 |
| 14-30 days | -$0.05 to -$0.08 |
| 7-14 days | -$0.08 to -$0.15 |
| 3-7 days | -$0.15 to -$0.30 |
| 0-3 days | -$0.30 to -$0.60 |

# INTRINSIC VS EXTRINSIC: VISUAL EXAMPLES

## Example 1: Deep In-the-Money Call

SPY at $590, $575 call trading at $18.50, 7 days left

Intrinsic: $590 - $575 = $15.00

Extrinsic: $18.50 - $15.00 = $3.50

Breakdown: 81% intrinsic, 19% extrinsic

Why this matters: Deep ITM options move almost 1:1 with stock (high Delta ~0.90). Less theta risk.

## Example 2: At-the-Money Call

SPY at $575, $575 call trading at $4.20, 7 days left

Intrinsic: $575 - $575 = $0.00

Extrinsic: $4.20 - $0.00 = $4.20

Breakdown: 0% intrinsic, 100% extrinsic

Why this matters: ATM options are pure time value. High theta risk. Stock must move quickly or theta destroys value.

## Example 3: Out-of-the-Money Call

SPY at $575, $585 call trading at $0.65, 7 days left

Intrinsic: $0 (OTM has no intrinsic)

Extrinsic: $0.65

Breakdown: 0% intrinsic, 100% extrinsic

Why this matters: OTM options are lottery tickets. Need big move (+$10) to profit. High risk, low probability.

# CHEAP VS EXPENSIVE OPTIONS

## What Makes an Option "Expensive"?

An option is expensive when extrinsic value is high relative to probability of profit. This happens when:

•Implied volatility is elevated (IV Rank >75)

•Too much time premium for likelihood of move

•Market expects big move that may not happen

Example:

SPY $575 call, 7 days, IV 25% (high), premium $6.80

Same option with normal IV 15%: $4.20

You are overpaying $2.60 (62%) for elevated IV

## What Makes an Option "Cheap"?

An option is cheap when extrinsic value is low relative to probability. This happens when:

•Implied volatility is low (IV Rank <25)

•Time to expiration is short (but not 0DTE)

•Market underestimates potential move

Example:

SPY $575 call, 7 days, IV 12% (low), premium $3.50

This is 17% cheaper than "normal" $4.20 pricing

Good time to buy (if setup is right)

# FAQ

### Why does my option lose money when stock moves sideways?

Time decay (theta). Every day that passes, extrinsic value decreases. If stock does not move enough to offset theta, you lose money even with no stock movement.

### Can intrinsic value decay?

No. Intrinsic value only changes with stock price. Only extrinsic value decays over time. Deep in-the-money options have minimal theta because they are mostly intrinsic value.

### Why do far OTM options cost so little?

Low probability of finishing in-the-money. Market prices in <10% chance. All extrinsic value, and very little of it. They are cheap because they usually expire worthless.

### How do I know if premium is too high?

Check IV Rank. If >75, premium is expensive. Compare current IV to historical average. If current is 50% above average, wait for IV to drop before buying.

### Do options ever trade below intrinsic value?

Rarely, and only deep in-the-money options with high theta. Example: $575 call with stock at $600, 1 day left, might trade at $24.80 (intrinsic $25) due to exercise costs. Not common.

### Should I focus on cheap or expensive options?

Neither. Focus on probability. A "cheap" $0.15 OTM option is expensive if probability is 2%. A "expensive" $4.20 ATM option is cheap if setup has 70% win rate. Price without probability is meaningless.

📝 OPTIONS EARNINGS PLAYS STRATEGY

OPTIONS EARNINGS PLAYS STRATEGY

Complete Guide to Trading Options Around Earnings

# SEO METADATA

URL: /options-earnings-plays-strategy

Title (59): Options Earnings Plays Strategy: Complete Guide 2026

Meta Description (160): Learn how to trade options around earnings announcements. Understand IV expansion, earnings straddles, post-earnings momentum, IV crush protection, and when to exit.

Primary KW: options earnings plays

Secondary KW: earnings options strategy, trading earnings with options, earnings straddle, earnings IV crush

# INTRODUCTION

⚠️ EARNINGS TRADING: HIGH REWARD, HIGH RISK

Earnings announcements create explosive 5-15% stock moves in minutes. Options can return 100-300% overnight. But IV crush destroys 50-70% of option value instantly if you hold through the announcement.

This guide teaches you how to profit from earnings volatility while avoiding the traps that wipe out accounts.

# WHAT HAPPENS DURING EARNINGS

## The Earnings Cycle

Earnings announcements follow a predictable 4-phase pattern:

Phase 1: Pre-Earnings IV Expansion (7-14 days before)

Implied volatility rises as uncertainty increases. Option premiums get expensive. Stock consolidates.

Phase 2: Maximum IV (1-2 days before)

IV peaks at 60-120% (vs normal 30-50%). Options at peak pricing. Expectation is "priced in."

Phase 3: Earnings Release (After close or before open)

Stock gaps 3-15% in seconds. Options explode in value if correct direction. IV crashes -30 to -50%.

Phase 4: Post-Earnings Stabilization (1-3 days after)

IV returns to normal. Stock finds new range. Momentum trades emerge.

## Example: NVIDIA Earnings Cycle

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Phase | Date | Stock Price | IV |
| Pre-Earnings | Feb 10 | $850 | 35% |
| IV Expansion | Feb 17 | $848 | 65% |
| Max IV | Feb 20 (day before) | $851 | 82% |
| Earnings (after close) | Feb 21 4:15 PM | $920 (+8.1%) | 38% |
| Post-Earnings | Feb 24 | $915 | 40% |

Notice: IV spiked from 35% to 82% (+134%), then crashed to 38% (-54%) after earnings. This is the pattern.

# EARNINGS TRADING STRATEGIES

## Strategy 1: Pre-Earnings IV Expansion Play

Buy options 7-14 days before earnings, sell 1-2 days before announcement to capture IV rise without IV crush risk.

Setup:

•Earnings in 10 days, IV currently low (IV Rank <30)

•Buy ATM or slightly ITM calls/puts

•Weekly or bi-weekly expiration (includes earnings date)

•Target: +40-80% from IV expansion alone

•Exit: 1-2 days before earnings (avoid the crush)

Example:

Feb 10: NVDA earnings Feb 21 (11 days away), IV 35%, stock $850

Buy NVDA $850 call expiring Feb 23 for $32.00

Feb 19 (2 days before earnings): IV now 75%, call worth $48.00

Sell for +50% profit WITHOUT holding through earnings

Stock barely moved ($850→$851), but IV expansion created profit

OnlyOptions Performance:

Pre-earnings IV plays: 73% win rate, +52% average winner, hold time 8 days

## Strategy 2: Earnings Straddle (Hold Through)

Buy both a call and a put, profit if stock makes big move either direction. High risk, high reward.

Setup:

•Buy ATM call + ATM put simultaneously

•1-2 hours before earnings announcement

•Exit immediately after announcement (within 1 hour)

•Requires 5%+ stock move to overcome IV crush

Example:

Feb 21, 3:00 PM: NVDA earnings at 4:15 PM, stock $851

Buy NVDA $850 call for $41.00

Buy NVDA $850 put for $39.00

Total cost: $80.00 ($8,000 per straddle)

Breakeven: Stock must move >$80 either direction (9.4%)

Scenario A: NVDA beats, rallies to $920 (+8.1%)

Call worth $70.00 (stock up but IV crushed), Put worth $0

Exit immediately: $70 vs $80 entry = -$10 loss (-12.5%)

Scenario B: NVDA beats, rallies to $960 (+12.8%)

Call worth $110.00, Put worth $0

Exit immediately: $110 vs $80 entry = +$30 profit (+37.5%)

Key Insight:

Stock must move BIGGER than expected. If market expects 8% move (priced into IV), you need 12%+ to profit. Difficult.

OnlyOptions Performance:

Earnings straddles: 48% win rate, +87% average winner, -68% average loser. High variance.

## Strategy 3: Post-Earnings Momentum Play

Wait for earnings, watch stock reaction, then trade momentum in the new direction. Safest approach.

Setup:

•Earnings announced, stock gaps 5%+ up or down

•Wait 30-60 minutes for initial volatility to settle

•Buy calls if gapped up + holding gains, or puts if gapped down

•Target: Ride 2-3 day continuation

•Exit: 1-3 days later

Example:

Feb 21, 4:15 PM: NVDA reports blowout earnings, stock gaps $850→$920

Feb 22, 10:30 AM: Stock holds $915-$925 range (momentum confirmed)

Buy NVDA $920 call expiring Feb 28 for $18.00

Feb 24: Stock continues to $945, exit call at $31.00 (+72%)

Why This Works:

IV already crushed (options are cheap now). You are playing pure price movement, not volatility. Lower risk.

OnlyOptions Performance:

Post-earnings momentum: 69% win rate, +78% average winner, 2.8 day hold

## Strategy 4: Sell Premium (Advanced Only)

Sell options to collect inflated premiums, profit from IV crush. Requires Level 3+ approval. High risk.

Setup:

•Sell OTM call + put (strangle) 1-2 days before earnings

•Collect $6,000-$12,000 premium

•Stock must stay within range for profit

•Risk: Unlimited if stock moves far

This strategy is NOT recommended for beginners. Requires $25K+ account and deep options knowledge.

# IV CRUSH — THE EARNINGS KILLER

## Understanding the Crush

IV crush is when implied volatility drops 30-70% immediately after earnings, destroying option value even if stock moves favorably.

Why It Happens:

Before earnings: Uncertainty = high IV = expensive options

After earnings: Uncertainty gone = low IV = cheap options

The "event risk" is removed, so volatility collapses

## IV Crush Examples

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Company | Stock Move | IV Before | IV After |
| NVDA | +8.1% | 82% | 38% (-54%) |
| AAPL | +3.2% | 45% | 22% (-51%) |
| TSLA | +12.4% | 95% | 48% (-49%) |
| AMZN | -5.1% | 68% | 35% (-49%) |

Average IV crush: -50%. Even big stock moves (8-12%) struggle to overcome 50% IV loss.

## Protecting Against IV Crush

Method 1: Exit Before Earnings

Sell your position 1 day before announcement. Capture IV expansion, avoid crush entirely. Safest method.

Method 2: Use Spreads

Buy call, sell higher call = spread. Both legs crushed equally. Net IV exposure = zero. Lower profit but protected.

Method 3: Buy Post-Earnings

Wait until after earnings. IV already crushed, options are cheap. Play momentum without IV risk.

Method 4: Only Hold If Massive Move Expected

If you expect 15%+ move (rare), IV crush may not matter. Still risky. Use 1% position size, not 2%.

# BEST STOCKS FOR EARNINGS PLAYS

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Ticker | Avg Earnings Move | IV Spike | Best Strategy |
| NVDA | 8-12% | +100% | Pre-earnings IV |
| TSLA | 10-15% | +80% | Post-momentum |
| AAPL | 3-6% | +40% | Pre-earnings IV |
| AMZN | 6-10% | +60% | Post-momentum |
| META | 8-14% | +90% | Straddle (risky) |

# EARNINGS CALENDAR AND TIMING

## When Earnings Are Announced

Most earnings: After market close (4:00 PM ET) or before market open (7:30 AM ET)

After-Hours Earnings (Most Common):

Announced: 4:00-5:00 PM ET

Stock moves: 4:00-8:00 PM ET (extended hours)

Options settle: Next morning 9:30 AM

Strategy: Exit positions by 9:45 AM next day

Pre-Market Earnings:

Announced: 6:30-8:00 AM ET

Stock moves: 8:00-9:30 AM (pre-market)

Options open: 9:30 AM

Strategy: Exit by 10:30 AM same day

## Finding Earnings Dates

Free resources:

•Earnings Whispers (earningswhispers.com)

•Yahoo Finance (finance.yahoo.com)

•Your broker (most show upcoming earnings)

•OnlyOptions earnings calendar (members only)

# COMMON EARNINGS MISTAKES

Mistake #1: Holding Through Without Plan

You buy options "hoping" for good earnings. No exit plan. IV crushes you. Always have exit plan BEFORE earnings.

Mistake #2: Buying Day of Earnings

IV already at peak. You pay maximum price. Stock must move 10%+ to profit. Bad odds. Enter early or wait until after.

Mistake #3: Ignoring Historical Earnings Moves

AAPL typically moves 3-4% on earnings. You buy straddle requiring 8% move. Unrealistic. Check historical averages first.

Mistake #4: Over-Sizing Positions

Earnings are volatile. Use 1% risk (not 2%) on earnings plays. Protect capital from unexpected outcomes.

# FAQ

### Should beginners trade earnings?

Not recommended. Earnings require understanding IV, Greeks, and timing. Trade at least 50 regular options first. Then start with post-earnings momentum (safest strategy).

### What is the safest earnings strategy?

Post-earnings momentum. Wait for announcement, let IV crush happen, then buy cheap options to ride 2-3 day continuation. 69% win rate, lower stress.

### How much can I make on earnings?

Pre-earnings IV expansion: +40-80% typical. Earnings straddles: +100-300% if big move, -60-80% if wrong. Post-earnings momentum: +60-100% typical. High variance.

### Do OnlyOptions signals include earnings plays?

Yes. We send pre-earnings IV expansion plays (1-2 weeks before) and post-earnings momentum plays (day after). We do NOT send straddles (too risky for most members). Earnings plays = 8% of total signals.

### Can I trade earnings in IRA?

Yes, if your IRA has options approval. However, straddles require buying 2 options = double capital. Stick to single-leg strategies (pre-earnings calls/puts, post-earnings momentum).

### What happens if earnings are delayed?

Rare but possible. If company delays earnings, IV stays elevated. Your option loses value to theta decay while waiting. Set a time stop: If no earnings within 3 days of expected date, exit position.

📝 10 MOST COMMON OPTIONS TRADING MISTAKES

10 MOST COMMON OPTIONS TRADING MISTAKES

And How to Avoid Account-Destroying Errors

# SEO METADATA

URL: /common-options-trading-mistakes

Title (58): 10 Common Options Trading Mistakes to Avoid \| OnlyOptions

Meta Description (160): Learn the 10 most common options trading mistakes that destroy accounts. Understand why traders fail, how to avoid costly errors, and what to do instead for success.

Primary KW: options trading mistakes

Secondary KW: common options mistakes, why traders fail, options trading errors, avoid options mistakes

# INTRODUCTION

95% of options traders lose money. Not because they pick bad stocks. Not because they lack intelligence. They lose because they repeat the same 10 mistakes over and over.

This guide identifies the most common options trading mistakes, explains why they destroy accounts, and shows you exactly what to do instead.

# MISTAKE \#1: NOT USING STOP-LOSSES

❌ MISTAKE: "I Will Just Watch It and Exit Manually"

You buy a call at $2.40. It drops to $2.00. You think "it will bounce." It drops to $1.50. You think "surely now." It drops to $0.75. You finally panic sell at $0.60.

Loss: -75% (-$180 per contract)

Why This Kills Accounts:

Emotions override logic. Hope replaces strategy. One -75% loss requires +300% gain to recover. After 3-4 of these, your account is destroyed.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

Set stop-loss immediately after entry. Place actual order in broker (GTC limit order). Example: Entry $2.40, stop $1.65. If hit, you lose -31% (-$75), not -75% (-$180). Preserve capital, live to trade another day.

# MISTAKE \#2: POSITION SIZING TOO LARGE

❌ MISTAKE: Risking 10-20% Per Trade

You have $10,000. You risk $2,000 on one "sure thing" trade. It loses. Now you have $8,000. You risk $1,600 to "recover." It loses. Now $6,400. Three losses = -36% of account.

Why This Kills Accounts:

Math of drawdowns: -20% + -20% + -20% = -48.8% (not -60%). Recovery requires +95% gain. Impossible.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

2% rule, always. $10,000 account = $200 max risk per trade. Twenty losses = down 33%, still recoverable. Sleep at night.

# MISTAKE \#3: BUYING FAR OUT-OF-THE-MONEY OPTIONS

❌ MISTAKE: "These $0.15 Calls Are Cheap — Huge Upside!"

SPY at $575. You buy $590 calls for $0.15 because "if SPY hits $595, these will be worth $5.00!"

Reality: SPY needs +2.6% move. Happens 5% of the time. 95% of the time, expires worthless.

Why This Kills Accounts:

Cheap options are cheap for a reason: low probability. Buying 10 lottery tickets at $0.15 = $150 wasted. Even one winner (+$400) does not offset 9 losers.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

Buy at-the-money (ATM) or 1-2 strikes out-of-the-money maximum. SPY $575, buy $575 or $577 calls, not $590. Higher cost but 60-70% probability vs 5%.

# MISTAKE \#4: HOLDING OPTIONS UNTIL EXPIRATION

❌ MISTAKE: "I Will Hold Until Friday to Maximize Profit"

Monday: Buy $575 call for $2.40, up to $3.50 (+46%) by Wednesday. You hold for "more gains." Thursday: $3.20. Friday 3 PM: $2.80. Expires at $2.70.

Final result: +13% instead of +46%.

Why This Kills Accounts:

Time decay accelerates in final 3 days. Gamma risk explodes in final hours. Holding for extra 10% costs you 30% when theta burns value.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

Exit 2-3 days before expiration. For 0DTE, exit by 3:30 PM. Take profits at 50-75% gain, do not wait for 100%. Greed kills.

# MISTAKE \#5: IGNORING IMPLIED VOLATILITY

❌ MISTAKE: Buying Options Without Checking IV

Stock looks bullish. You buy calls. Stock rises 3%. Your calls... lose money?

Why: IV was 80% (extremely high). After you bought, IV dropped to 50% (IV crush). Vega loss exceeded Delta gain.

Why This Kills Accounts:

Overpaying by 30-50% due to high IV. Even correct directional trades lose money. Repeated overpaying = slow death.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

Check IV Rank before every trade. <25 = good time to buy. >75 = wait or skip. Never buy options when IV Rank >80 unless specific edge.

# MISTAKE \#6: TRADING WITHOUT A PLAN

❌ MISTAKE: "I Will Figure It Out After I Buy"

You see SPY moving up, FOMO kicks in, you buy a call. No target, no stop, no thesis. It moves against you. You panic sell at -40%.

Why This Kills Accounts:

No plan = reactive trading = emotional decisions = losses. Every trade without a plan is a gamble, not a strategy.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

Before clicking buy, answer:

•Why am I entering? (Technical setup, catalyst, signal)

•Where is my stop-loss? (Exact price)

•Where is my profit target? (Exact price)

•How long will I hold? (Hours, days, weeks)

•What is my risk-reward ratio? (Minimum 2:1)

No answers? No trade.

# MISTAKE \#7: AVERAGING DOWN ON LOSING POSITIONS

❌ MISTAKE: "Buy More to Lower My Average"

Buy 2 contracts at $2.40. Price drops to $1.50. You buy 2 more to "average down" to $1.95. Stop-loss at $1.20 now loses 4 × ($1.95 - $1.20) × 100 = $300 instead of planned $200.

Why This Kills Accounts:

Turns controlled losses into catastrophic losses. Options expire — they do not recover like stocks. Doubling down on losers violates risk management.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

Never add to losing positions. If wrong, take the loss and move on. Only add to winners (scaling in). Protect capital above all else.

# MISTAKE \#8: TRADING 0DTE TOO SOON

❌ MISTAKE: Starting With Same-Day Expiration

First week trading options, you try 0DTE because "huge profits in hours!" You lose 7 out of 10 trades due to extreme theta decay, whipsaws, and lack of experience. Account down -40% in one week.

Why This Kills Accounts:

0DTE requires experience with Greeks, technical analysis, and emotional control. Beginners do not have these. Starting with 0DTE = starting golf at PGA Tour.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

No 0DTE for first 6 months. Start with monthly options (30 days), then weekly (7 days), then 0DTE after 20+ profitable trades. Build skills before speed.

# MISTAKE \#9: OVER-TRADING

❌ MISTAKE: "I Must Take Every Signal to Make Money"

You take 8 trades per day. Half violate your risk rules. You cannot track them all. You miss stop-losses. You overtrade your account. Three losers happen simultaneously = -15% day.

Why This Kills Accounts:

Quality > quantity. Over-trading leads to mistakes, rule violations, and correlation risk (all positions move against you at once). Death by a thousand cuts.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

Maximum 2-3 positions open at once. Total portfolio heat <8%. Skip trades that do not meet all criteria. Say NO to mediocre setups. One great trade > five average trades.

# MISTAKE \#10: REVENGE TRADING AFTER LOSSES

❌ MISTAKE: "I Need to Make It Back Right Now"

You lose -$500 on a bad trade. Angry, you immediately enter another trade with $1,000 risk to "recover faster." It also loses. Now down -$1,500. You chase again. Spiral continues.

Why This Kills Accounts:

Emotions control decisions. Revenge trading = gambling. You violate position sizing, ignore stop-losses, trade bad setups. Fastest way to blow up account.

✅ CORRECT APPROACH:

After any loss (especially >$200), take 30-minute break. Walk away from screen. Review what went wrong. Only enter next trade when calm and trade meets all criteria. Never chase losses.

# BONUS MISTAKES (QUICK LIST)

## Mistake \#11: Using Market Orders on Options

Wide bid-ask spreads destroy you. Always use limit orders.

## Mistake \#12: Not Understanding Greeks

Trading without knowing Delta, Theta, Vega = flying blind. Read our Greeks guide.

## Mistake \#13: Trading During First 30 Minutes

9:30-10:00 AM = chaos, wide spreads, fake moves. Wait until 10:00 AM.

## Mistake \#14: Forgetting to Roll Stops to Breakeven

Up +40%? Move stop to breakeven. Protect gains.

## Mistake \#15: Trading Illiquid Options

Volume <500 contracts/day = wide spreads, poor fills, stuck holding. Stick to SPY/QQQ.

# THE ONE RULE THAT PREVENTS ALL MISTAKES

Every mistake above comes from breaking one fundamental rule:

|     |
| --- |
| FOLLOW YOUR SYSTEM, IGNORE YOUR EMOTIONS |

You know stop-losses work. You know 2% risk protects you. You know cheap OTM options fail. Yet you violate these rules when emotions take over.

The Solution:

Write down your rules. Before every trade, check: "Am I following my rules?" If no, do not trade. Save the checklist. Review after every loss.

# ONLYOPTIONS HELPS YOU AVOID MISTAKES

## How Our Signals Prevent Errors

Stop-Losses Included:

Every signal has exact stop-loss price. No guessing.

Position Sizing Calculated:

We tell you how many contracts based on 2% rule.

Only High-Probability Setups:

No far OTM lottery tickets. ATM or 1-2 strikes out only.

We tell you when to exit. No holding until expiration.

We screen out expensive options (high IV Rank >75).

Entry, target, stop, rationale — all included. No guessing.

Following our signals eliminates 8 of the 10 mistakes above. The other 2 (revenge trading, over-trading) require your discipline.

# FAQ

### I made all these mistakes. Can I still succeed?

Yes. Most profitable traders lost money in their first 6-12 months. The key is learning from mistakes, not repeating them. If you recognize these mistakes now, you are ahead of 90% of traders.

### What is the \#1 mistake that kills most accounts?

Not using stop-losses. This single mistake destroys more accounts than anything else. One -80% loss can erase months of +20% wins. Always use stops.

### How do I stop revenge trading?

Set a rule: After any loss, 30-minute mandatory break. No exceptions. Walk away, drink water, reset emotions. Only trade again when calm. Install a timer if needed.

### Can I break the 2% rule if I am very confident?

No. Confidence is irrelevant. Even 90% probability trades lose 10% of the time. The 2% rule exists for that 10%. Stick to it always.

### Is it okay to average down on winners?

Adding to winners (scaling in) is fine IF total position still respects 2% rule. Example: Buy 1 contract, up +30%, add 1 more = 2 total risk still <2%. Never exceed 2% total.

### How long until I stop making these mistakes?

Depends on discipline. Some traders fix mistakes in 3 months. Others never do. Key: Keep a trade journal, review mistakes weekly, adjust rules, repeat. Improvement comes from awareness + action.

📝 WEEKLY VS MONTHLY OPTIONS GUIDE

WEEKLY VS MONTHLY OPTIONS GUIDE

When to Use Each Expiration for Maximum Profits

# SEO METADATA

URL: /weekly-vs-monthly-options-guide

Title (58): Weekly vs Monthly Options: Which Should You Trade? 2026

Meta Description (160): Learn the difference between weekly and monthly options. Understand time decay, cost differences, best use cases, and when to choose 7-day vs 30-day expirations for options trading.

Primary KW: weekly vs monthly options

Secondary KW: weekly options trading, monthly options strategy, 0dte vs weekly, best option expiration

# INTRODUCTION

# Expiration Matters More Than Most Traders Think

Choosing the right expiration date is as important as picking the right strike price. Weekly options offer speed and lower cost but high risk. Monthly options provide time and flexibility but higher cost and slower theta.

This guide breaks down weekly vs monthly options, when to use each, and how OnlyOptions structures signals around different expirations.

# QUICK COMPARISON TABLE

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Feature | 0DTE | Weekly (7 days) | Monthly (30 days) |
| Time Decay | Extreme | Fast | Slow |
| Cost | $100-300 | $300-600 | $800-1,500 |
| Profit Potential | 50-100% | 60-100% | 50-120% |
| Holding Period | 2-4 hours | 1-5 days | 1-3 weeks |
| Risk Level | Very High | High | Moderate |
| Best For | Scalpers | Swing traders | Trend followers |
| Win Rate | 60-70% | 65-75% | 60-70% |

# WEEKLY OPTIONS (7-14 DAYS TO EXPIRATION)

## What Are Weekly Options?

Weekly options expire every Friday (standard weeklies). SPY and QQQ also offer Monday/Wednesday expirations. Typical holding period: 1-5 days.

## Advantages of Weekly Options

1\. Lower Cost

SPY $575 call, 7 days out: ~$4.00 ($400 per contract)

Same strike, 30 days out: ~$9.00 ($900 per contract)

Weeklies cost 40-60% less than monthlies.

2\. Fast Profits

Capture 60-100% gains in 1-3 days. Perfect for momentum plays and swing trades.

3\. Multiple Opportunities

New weekly expiration every Friday. Fresh chances every week vs monthly once per month.

4\. Lower Capital Requirements

$400 per contract (weekly) vs $900 (monthly) = trade more signals with same capital.

## Disadvantages of Weekly Options

1\. Faster Time Decay

Theta burns -$0.08 to -$0.15 per day. If stock does not move quickly, you lose money.

2\. Less Forgiveness

Stock moves against you for 2 days? With 30-day option, you have 28 days to recover. With 7-day, you are already down 30% to theta.

3\. Higher Stress

Constant monitoring. Every day matters. No time to "wait and see."

## When to Use Weekly Options

Use weeklies when:

•You expect strong directional move within 3-5 days

•Technical setup is clear (breakout, earnings momentum, Fed reaction)

•You can monitor position daily

•You want to maximize capital efficiency (trade more signals)

•Trend is already in motion (not waiting for reversal)

OnlyOptions Weekly Signals:

40% of our signals are weekly options. Win rate: 72.5%. Average hold: 2.8 days. Target profit: 60-100%.

# MONTHLY OPTIONS (30-45 DAYS TO EXPIRATION)

## What Are Monthly Options?

Monthly options expire the 3rd Friday of each month. Typical holding period: 1-3 weeks.

## Advantages of Monthly Options

1\. Time to Be Right

Stock drops 5% in week 1? You have 3 more weeks for recovery. Weeklies would already be dead.

2\. Slower Time Decay

Theta -$0.03 to -$0.05 per day (vs -$0.15 for weeklies). Less daily stress.

3\. Ride Longer Trends

Capture 2-3 week uptrends or downtrends. Weeklies force you to exit early.

4\. Less Monitoring Required

Check once or twice daily instead of every hour. Better for people with jobs.

## Disadvantages of Monthly Options

1\. Higher Cost

$900 per contract vs $400 for weeklies. Requires larger account or fewer trades.

2\. Slower Profits

Takes 1-2 weeks to hit 70-100% targets vs 2-4 days for weeklies.

3\. More Capital Tied Up

$900 locked per contract for weeks. Reduces ability to take new signals.

4\. Larger Losses on Stop-Outs

Stop-loss at -30% = lose $270 per contract (monthly) vs $120 (weekly).

## When to Use Monthly Options

Use monthlies when:

•Technical setup needs time to develop (consolidation, basing)

•Trend is forming but not fully established yet

•You cannot monitor daily (full-time job, family commitments)

•Market is choppy (needs time for direction to clarify)

•You prefer lower stress, slower pace

OnlyOptions Monthly Signals:

30% of our signals are monthly options. Win rate: 71.8%. Average hold: 11 days. Target profit: 70-120%.

# DIRECT COMPARISON — SAME TRADE

## Example: SPY Bullish Breakout

SPY at $575, breaking above resistance, target $585

Weekly Option (7 days to expiration):

Buy SPY $575 call for $4.20

Target: $7.50 (+79%)

Stop: $2.75 (-35%)

Hold: 3 days

Theta risk: -$0.12/day

Result: SPY hits $582 in 3 days, exit at $7.80 (+86%)

Monthly Option (30 days to expiration):

Buy SPY $575 call for $9.50

Target: $16.00 (+68%)

Stop: $6.50 (-32%)

Hold: 8 days

Theta risk: -$0.04/day

Result: SPY hits $582 in 8 days, exit at $16.20 (+71%)

Analysis:

Weekly: Higher % return (+86% vs +71%), faster (3 days vs 8 days), but higher theta risk.

Monthly: Safer (more time), lower stress, but more capital ($950 vs $420), slower profit.

# COMBINING WEEKLY AND MONTHLY IN YOUR PORTFOLIO

## The 60/40 Strategy

Allocate 60% of capital to weekly options, 40% to monthly:

•Weekly 60%: Capture fast moves, high turnover, frequent profits

•Monthly 40%: Long-term trends, stability, lower stress

This balances speed with safety. Weekly profits fund monthly positions.

## The Beginner Strategy

If new to options (<6 months):

•80% monthly, 20% weekly

•Monthly gives you time to learn, make mistakes, recover

•Weekly teaches you urgency and timing

## The Aggressive Strategy

If experienced (1+ year):

•20% monthly, 50% weekly, 30% 0DTE

•Maximize turnover and profit velocity

•Requires constant monitoring and tight discipline

# TIME DECAY COMPARISON

## Theta Decay by Days to Expiration

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Days to Expiration | Daily Theta | % Value Lost/Day |
| 0 (same day) | -$0.30 to -$0.50 | 15-25% |
| 3 days | -$0.20 to -$0.30 | 8-12% |
| 7 days (weekly) | -$0.08 to -$0.15 | 2-4% |
| 14 days | -$0.05 to -$0.10 | 1-2% |
| 30 days (monthly) | -$0.03 to -$0.05 | 0.3-0.6% |
| 60 days | -$0.02 to -$0.03 | 0.2-0.3% |

Notice: Theta accelerates as expiration approaches. 0-7 days is danger zone. 30+ days is safe zone.

# COST COMPARISON — REAL NUMBERS

## SPY $575 Call Example (Stock at $575)

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Expiration | Premium | Total Cost (1 contract) |
| 0DTE | $1.80 | $180 |
| 3 days | $2.90 | $290 |
| 7 days (weekly) | $4.20 | $420 |
| 14 days | $6.00 | $600 |
| 30 days (monthly) | $9.50 | $950 |
| 60 days | $13.00 | $1,300 |

Key insight: Moving from 7-day to 30-day costs 2.26x more. But you get 4.3x more time. Monthly is MORE capital-efficient per day of time.

# WHICH EXPIRATION FOR WHICH STRATEGY?

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Strategy Type | Best Expiration | Why |
| Breakout/Momentum | Weekly | Fast move expected, capitalize quickly |
| Trend Following | Monthly | Ride multi-week trends |
| Earnings Play | Weekly | Exit 1-2 days after earnings |
| Mean Reversion | 0DTE or Weekly | Quick bounce, fast exit |
| Consolidation Breakout | Monthly | Wait for pattern to resolve |
| High Volatility Environment | Weekly or 0DTE | Capitalize on big swings fast |
| Low Volatility Environment | Monthly | Need time for moves to develop |

Weekly options are our sweet spot — balance of speed, cost, and win rate.

# FAQ

### Should beginners use weekly or monthly options?

Monthly. Beginners need time to learn, make mistakes, and recover. Weekly options punish mistakes harshly with fast theta decay. After 6 months, add weeklies to your mix.

### Can I roll a weekly to a monthly if it is not working?

Yes, but usually not recommended. Rolling costs money (selling losing weekly, buying monthly). Better to take the small loss and wait for better setup. Avoid "hope trading."

### Why do weekly options sometimes outperform monthly?

Leverage. Weekly costs $400, monthly costs $900. For same dollar risk ($400), you get 1 monthly or 1 weekly. Weekly can move 100% in 3 days while monthly moves 50% in same time.

### Do OnlyOptions signals specify expiration?

Yes, always. Every signal includes exact expiration date. We analyze technical setup and choose optimal expiration (0DTE, weekly, or monthly) based on expected timing of move.

### Can I use monthly when signal says weekly?

Yes, but adjust expectations. Monthly will profit less % but give you more time. If you cannot monitor daily or want lower stress, monthly is acceptable substitute.

### What is the worst expiration to trade?

Options with 1-3 days left (not 0DTE). Too much theta decay, not enough time to be right, and not cheap like 0DTE. Avoid "dead zone" of 1-3 days unless specifically signaled.

📝 UNDERSTANDING IMPLIED VOLATILITY (IV)

UNDERSTANDING IMPLIED VOLATILITY (IV)

Complete Guide to IV and Why It Matters for Options Trading

# SEO METADATA

URL: /understanding-implied-volatility-options

Title (60): Implied Volatility Explained: IV Guide for Options Trading

Meta Description (158): Learn what implied volatility (IV) is, how it affects option prices, IV crush after earnings, IV rank vs percentile, and how to trade high/low IV environments effectively.

Primary KW: implied volatility options

Secondary KW: what is IV, implied volatility explained, IV crush, high IV low IV, IV rank options

# INTRODUCTION

# Why Your Option Loses Money When the Stock Moves Your Way

You buy a call. The stock rises. Your option... loses money? Welcome to implied volatility (IV) — the invisible force that controls option prices.

IV determines how expensive or cheap options are. Understanding IV prevents costly mistakes like holding through earnings (IV crush) or buying overpriced options. This guide explains everything.

# WHAT IS IMPLIED VOLATILITY?

## Simple Definition

Implied volatility is the market's expectation of how much a stock will move in the future. High IV = market expects big moves. Low IV = market expects small moves.

Important:

IV is NOT about past movement. It is about expected future movement. It is "implied" from current option prices.

## Real-World Analogy

Think of IV like insurance premiums. When a hurricane approaches Florida, home insurance becomes expensive (high IV). When weather is calm, insurance is cheap (low IV). Option premiums work the same way — high uncertainty = high cost.

## How IV Affects Option Prices

Higher IV = Higher option premiums

Lower IV = Lower option premiums

Example:

SPY at $575, 30 days to expiration

Low IV (12%): $575 call costs $3.50

High IV (25%): Same $575 call costs $6.80

The stock price did not change, but the option is nearly 2x more expensive due to IV.

# IV LEVELS — WHAT IS HIGH VS LOW?

|     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Ticker | Low IV | Normal IV | High IV |
| SPY | <12% | 12-18% | >20% |
| QQQ | <15% | 18-25% | >28% |
| NVDA | <35% | 40-60% | >70% |
| TSLA | <45% | 50-70% | >80% |

IV levels are relative to the stock. TSLA at 50% IV is normal. SPY at 50% IV would be extreme panic.

# IV RANK AND IV PERCENTILE

## What is IV Rank?

IV Rank compares current IV to the past 52 weeks (1 year).

Formula: IV Rank = (Current IV - 52-week Low) ÷ (52-week High - 52-week Low) × 100

Example:

SPY current IV: 18%

52-week low: 10%

52-week high: 30%

IV Rank: (18 - 10) ÷ (30 - 10) × 100 = 40

IV Rank 40 = Current IV is at 40th percentile of past year.

## IV Rank Interpretation

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IV Rank | Meaning | Action |
| 0-25 | Very Low IV | Good time to buy options |
| 25-50 | Below Average | Decent time to buy |
| 50-75 | Above Average | Be cautious buying |
| 75-100 | Very High IV | Avoid buying (expensive) |

# IV CRUSH — THE OPTION KILLER

## What is IV Crush?

IV crush happens when implied volatility drops suddenly, causing option prices to plummet even if the stock moves in your favor. Most common after earnings announcements.

## Earnings IV Crush Example

NVDA trading at $850, earnings tomorrow

Before earnings: IV 80%, $870 call costs $18.00

Earnings beat, NVDA rallies to $875 (+$25)

After earnings: IV drops to 40% (crush), $870 call now worth $14.00

Result: Stock up $25, you LOSE $4.00 per share (-22%)

This is IV crush. The volatility expectation disappears after the event, destroying option value.

## How to Avoid IV Crush

Strategy 1: Exit Before Earnings

If you bought an option 1-2 weeks before earnings, sell the day before. Capture IV expansion, avoid IV crush.

Strategy 2: Buy Further-Dated Options

Monthly options (30+ days) have less IV exposure than weeklies. They survive IV crush better.

Strategy 3: Use Spreads

Vertical spreads (buy one option, sell another) reduce IV exposure. Both legs get crushed equally, offsetting the effect.

Strategy 4: Only Trade Earnings with Defined Risk

If trading through earnings, use small position sizes (1% risk, not 2%) because IV crush is unpredictable.

# TRADING HIGH IV VS LOW IV ENVIRONMENTS

## High IV Environment (VIX >25, SPY IV >18%)

Characteristics:

•Options are expensive (high premiums)

•Market uncertainty (Fed decisions, recession fears, geopolitical crisis)

•Big intraday swings (+/- 1-2%)

How to Trade:

•Avoid buying options (too expensive)

•Wait for IV to drop before entering positions

•If trading, use shorter expirations (0DTE, weekly) to minimize theta + vega exposure

•Expect higher win rates (big moves create profits) but also higher losses

## Low IV Environment (VIX <15, SPY IV <12%)

Characteristics:

•Options are cheap (low premiums)

•Market calm (no major catalysts)

•Small daily moves (+/- 0.3-0.5%)

How to Trade:

•Great time to buy options (cheap entry)

•Use longer expirations (weekly, monthly) — cheap theta

•Lower profit potential (stock moves less) but also lower loss risk

•Expect lower win rates (need bigger moves) but smaller losses

# VEGA — THE IV GREEK

## What is Vega?

Vega measures how much an option price changes when IV changes by 1%.

Vega 0.15 = Option gains $0.15 per 1% increase in IV

Vega 0.30 = Option gains $0.30 per 1% increase in IV

## Vega Example

SPY $575 call, 30 days out, Vega 0.20

Scenario 1: IV increases from 15% to 20% (+5%)

Option gains: 5 × 0.20 = +$1.00 per share (+$100 per contract)

Scenario 2: IV decreases from 15% to 10% (-5%)

Option loses: 5 × 0.20 = -$1.00 per share (-$100 per contract)

## Longer Expirations = Higher Vega

30-day options have more vega than 7-day options. 0DTE options have almost zero vega (no time for volatility to matter).

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Expiration | Typical Vega |
| 0DTE | 0.01 - 0.05 (minimal) |
| 7-day (weekly) | 0.08 - 0.15 |
| 30-day (monthly) | 0.15 - 0.30 |
| 90-day (quarterly) | 0.30 - 0.50 |

# PRACTICAL IV STRATEGIES

## Strategy 1: Buy Low IV, Sell High IV

When IV rank <25: Buy options (cheap entry)

When IV rank >75: Avoid buying (expensive) or sell spreads

## Strategy 2: Capture IV Expansion Before Events

Buy options 1-2 weeks before earnings. IV rises as earnings approach. Sell 1 day before earnings to capture IV expansion without IV crush risk.

## Strategy 3: Fade IV Spikes

VIX spikes to 35 on panic selling. SPY IV hits 25%. Wait 2-3 days for IV to normalize back to 15-18%, then buy calls (cheaper entry).

## Strategy 4: Use IV Rank for Position Sizing

IV Rank <30: Use full 2% position sizing

IV Rank 30-70: Use 1.5% position sizing

IV Rank >70: Use 1% position sizing or skip

# CHECKING IV BEFORE EVERY TRADE

## Where to Find IV

Your broker shows IV in the options chain:

•Thinkorswim: Options chain shows "IV" column

•Robinhood: Tap option, scroll to "Implied Volatility"

•Webull: Option details page shows IV%

## Pre-Trade IV Checklist

Before entering any options trade:

•Check current IV% (e.g., SPY at 16%)

•Check IV Rank (is it high or low relative to past year?)

•Check VIX (overall market volatility)

•Ask: Is this option expensive or cheap right now?

If IV Rank >70, seriously consider waiting for better entry or skipping the trade.

# COMMON IV MISTAKES

Mistake #1: Ignoring IV Entirely

You buy calls because "stock looks bullish" without checking IV. IV Rank is 95 (extremely expensive). You overpay by 30-50%. Even if stock moves your way, IV contraction erases gains.

Mistake #2: Holding Through Earnings for "Big Gains"

You think earnings will move stock 10%, so you hold. Stock moves 8% in your favor. IV crush destroys 12% of option value. Net: You lose money.

Mistake #3: Buying 0DTE on High IV Days

VIX at 30, SPY IV at 22%. You buy 0DTE calls. Even if SPY rises, theta + vega collapse destroy value. 0DTE already has minimal vega — high IV does not help.

Mistake #4: Confusing Historical Volatility with IV

Historical volatility (HV) = past movement. Implied volatility (IV) = expected future movement. They are different. IV is what matters for option pricing.

# FAQ

### What is a good IV to buy options?

IV Rank <25 is ideal. IV Rank 25-50 is acceptable. Above 50 means options are expensive — wait for IV to drop or skip the trade. Never buy when IV Rank >75 unless you have specific reason.

### Does IV affect 0DTE options?

Very little. 0DTE options have almost zero vega because there is no time for volatility to matter. Focus on delta and theta for 0DTE, not IV.

### How long does IV crush last after earnings?

Immediately. IV drops within seconds of earnings release. By next morning, new IV is established (usually 30-50% lower than pre-earnings). Full recovery can take 2-4 weeks.

### Can I profit from IV crush?

Yes, by selling options before earnings (advanced strategy). When you sell, you collect high premium. After IV crush, you buy back the option cheaper. This requires Level 3+ options approval.

### Why does IV spike on bad news but not good news?

Fear creates more volatility than greed. Market drops (bad news) trigger panic selling, spiking IV. Market rallies (good news) are orderly, so IV stays low. This is why VIX is called "fear index."

### Should I adjust position size based on IV?

Yes. High IV means options are expensive and prone to IV contraction. Reduce size to 1-1.5% instead of 2% when IV Rank >70. This protects you from overpaying.
